Current Commentary

Safeguarding Peace and Obstacles to Peace 26

—Ming

U.S. President Roosevelt, on the 16th of this month, proposed to the heads of state of 54 countries around the world to safeguard world peace, reiterating the essence of the Kellogg-Briand Pact. Its content can be roughly divided into the following three points. First, for the deployment of armaments, whether for defense or aggression, he implies serious criticism. And advocate the abolition of aggressive weapons. Second, to illustrate that the aggressive behavior of a country is enough to disturb world peace, therefore, "Each of the contracting states shall faithfully fulfill its obligations and shall each acknowledge that it will not send armed forces of any nature beyond its national borders." Third, he further declared that "Any country that does not participate with true sincerity will increase its armaments to an extent beyond that stipulated in the peace treaties, so that peace will ultimately be unsuccessful. … Then the civilized countries of the world will surely know where the responsibility for failure lies." Such a proposal is indeed the right medicine for the present, and a head-on warning to those engaged in military expansion and armed aggression.

The reason why such a globally sensational declaration was made before the opening of the World Economic Conference and after the initial end of the U.S. financial panic, seems in history to be contrary to the traditional claims of the United States. (Abandoning the Monroe Doctrine) And advocate international arms reduction, international economic cooperation, and communicate with Kalinin, chairman of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union, with whom the United States has not restored normal diplomatic relations. Not only did it break through historical traditions, but it also abandoned the dominance of temporary emotions, and sought peace between nations. This is why it is worthy of praise by all countries in the world. The President of the United States, in view of the urgency of the world situation and the revelation of the war crisis, and the economic panic, has deepened to the same degree as the deepening of the political crisis. Therefore, the market has become narrower and narrower, and international exchange has shrunk even more. As a result, the number of unemployed people has increased, people's hearts are uneasy, and society is turbulent and unsettled. This is indeed due to the evolution of the inherent contradictions of capitalism, which has led the rich to be "as wealthy as the Big Dipper," while the poor are "too poor to stand on their own feet." The purchasing power of the general public has declined, both at home and abroad. However, upon superficial observation, it is not so. Capitalism itself seems to still have room for development. If the countries of the world can truly cooperate and jointly seek a way to revive the world economy, then the future cannot be said to be absolutely hopeless. However, among the European capitalist countries, the hatred between Germany and France is firmly unbreakable. The former insists on abolishing the Treaty of Versailles and strongly advocates equality of armaments. The latter does not forget its "security guarantee," so it does its best to maintain the Treaty of Versailles. In addition, Italy, which is eyeing southern Europe, wants to dominate the Mediterranean. So it joined forces with Germany, Austria, Hungary and China, and called for a narrow fascist nationalism, which made Europe even more uneasy. The solution to the economic panic will become even more hopeless. Therefore, the U.S. President does not hesitate to sacrifice its "Monroe Doctrine" and advocate world arms reduction to eliminate the political crisis and seek international economic cooperation. Its painstaking efforts are truly commendable.

However, the Japanese militarists in the Far East have not fundamentally recognized the inherent inevitability of economic panic. Instead, they use the non-productive needs of the munitions industry to stimulate general industries and use inflationary policies to forcibly maintain the prosperity of the general economy in numerical terms. Therefore, it disregards international faith and tramples on the "Kellogg-Briand Pact" and all other international treaties. Under the guise of self-defense, it arbitrarily invaded the four northeastern provinces of our country, and created puppets by military force, claiming national self-determination, and in fact carrying out its armed aggression. Now it is even more rampant with its iron hooves, crossing the Luan River, crossing the Great Wall, and spying on Peiping and Tientsin, and disturbing North China. It wants to create its second pseudo-organization. Not only does it nominally destroy international peace, but it will also actually seize the interests of various countries in North China and carry out exclusive occupation. Therefore, the Japanese militarists are alone among the countries of the world, saying that the U.S.'s peace proposal only applies to Europe and not to East Asia, and they continue their armed aggression by sophistry with special circumstances. So how can President Roosevelt's declaration of peace and proposal for arms reduction not be shattered by the Japanese army?

Here, we know that those who are not equal in power are not enough to speak of peace, and those who are not equal in strength are not enough to maintain fairness. The power and strength of the United States in Europe are both barely equal. Therefore, there is room for negotiation for peace. What kind of grasp will it have in the Far East? We deeply sympathize with Roosevelt's declaration of peace and his application for arms reduction, but we are also worried that it will not be easy to succeed.

After Roosevelt's Declaration Was Released

The World Responds in Unison 27

Reply Letters from Ten Countries Delivered to the White House

Supporting the Proposal to Safeguard Peace

The U.S. Government Focuses Its Attention on the Development of the Situation in North China

Deeply Concerned That Japan Is Obstructing the Kellogg-Briand Pact

(Washington) The White House has received reply letters from Great Britain and nine other countries supporting the U.S. President's proposal to reduce armaments and seek peace and economic recovery. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Washington) Today, the White House and the State Department are both focusing their attention on the situation in North China, hoping for some development that can help the realization of the world's non-aggression pact. The atmosphere of the disarmament conference has now made significant progress, and the State Department anticipates that Japan will be the most likely to make reservations regarding this agreement. According to unofficial but reliable sources received by the State Department, Japan will be unlikely to accept this proposal until its position in Manchuria can be considered legal under international law. Also, according to news from Peiping and Tientsin, there is a possibility of a truce at this time. If a truce can be achieved, then the Japanese troops will withdraw to Manchuria, and a neutral zone will be demarcated between the Chinese and Japanese armies. If so, it may enable Japan to accept the non-aggression pact unconditionally. Therefore, the White House and the State Department are both paying attention to the development of the situation in North China. It is also heard that the State Department intends to have this agreement established before the opening of the World Economic Conference, but the wars in Manchuria and South America are major obstacles. It is deeply feared that unless the rumored truce in North China resolves the issue of the Japanese troops withdrawing from the South Manchurian Railway's attached lands, President Roosevelt's conditions will ultimately be difficult to fully achieve. As for South America, Paraguay and Bolivia, Peru and Colombia have not yet replied, nor have they expressed any opinions. As for Europe, since German Chancellor Hitler claimed that Germany would conclude a non-aggression treaty and guarantee not to forcibly break existing treaties, it is believed here that the disarmament crisis has been resolved. Furthermore, news that France heard Hitler's comparatively moderate wording and was relieved has also led to what is considered a hopeful phenomenon here. According to official sources, the U.S. President's desire is to conclude a world agreement with absolutely no reservations, because he feels that if there are any reservations, it will lose the original intention of his appeal. However, because Japan is an obstacle, this matter is feared to be extremely difficult to accomplish. (17th National News Agency Dispatch)

Our Country Is Preparing

To Accept Unconditionally 28

Reply Letter Is Being Drafted

Will Be Sent Out Today

(Nanjing) Roosevelt's application letter, published on the 16th, was sent to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs by the Counselor of the U.S. Embassy on the afternoon of the 17th. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs translated it into two copies, one sent to the National Government and forwarded to Chairman Lin in Xi'an, and the other presented to President Wang. The Central Committee held a special meeting for this purpose at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 18th. Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, Ju Zheng, Chen Guofu, Ye Chucang, Gu Mengyu, Chen Gongbo, Wang Shijie, He Yaozu, and others were present. Luo Wengan first gave a detailed report on the background and significance of the application. After careful discussion by the various dignitaries regarding our country's countermeasures, the meeting adjourned around 4:00 PM, deciding to answer Roosevelt in the name of Chairman Lin, unconditionally accepting his proposal in abstract terms. The reply letter will not mention the Far East issue, so the content will be extremely simple. Three people were designated at the meeting to draft the reply, and after a second meeting was held on the 19th to approve it, it will be sent out. (18th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Luo Wengan commented on Roosevelt's application letter, saying that U.S. President Roosevelt has far-sighted insight and advocates that all countries sincerely reduce their armaments and agree to prevent aggression, breaking the selfish and predatory situation and seeking progress for the world's long-term peace, which is admirable and congratulatory for the future of human happiness. However, Luo said that the world's arms race and expansion, as well as the aggressive actions of sacrificing neighboring countries to expand one's own territory, are in fact a minority, but based on our country's direct experience of aggression, it is deeply felt that even this minority of aggressors is more than enough to destroy the peace of the entire world. Therefore, the Chinese government and public believe that in order for world peace to be guaranteed, it is absolutely necessary to have Roosevelt's fourth step before being able to completely abolish offensive armaments. Roosevelt's proposed fourth step states that all countries in the world should participate in a solemn and definite non-aggression pact, each acknowledging that they will not send armed forces of any nature beyond their national borders. However, the Chinese government still has some concerns, because ambitious aggressor countries may not bow their heads and obey because of a solemn treaty. Those who obviously want to destroy world peace often do not consider what is called the responsibility and result of destruction. The peace conference of the European War is still vivid in our minds, but today the artillery fire of eastern Luan is fiercely and cruelly bombing without stopping. Therefore, we can no longer trust the so-called treaty obligations, etc. Wang Jingwei said about President Roosevelt's declaration that it is enough to open the door to world peace and is good news for mankind. (18th Dispatch)

U.S. Willing to Assist with Security Guarantees 29

Davis to Provide Additional Explanation

(Washington) It is heard that President Roosevelt intends, if the disarmament conference is successful, to have the United States assist in guaranteeing international security. As for the extent of U.S. involvement, he is now preparing to explain it. It is widely believed that U.S. Presidential Envoy Davis will make an announcement regarding this matter tomorrow in Geneva. The commitment made by the U.S. President must be approved by Congress to be effective. Currently, opposition within the U.S. to American involvement in foreign disputes appears quite strong. (Reuters, 18th)

France Expresses Gratification in Reply 30

(Paris) After President Roosevelt's letter to the heads of state of 54 nations attending the disarmament conference arrived in Paris, French President Lebrun immediately sent a reply by telegram, stating, "Your declaration issued in the name of the U.S. President has been received. I am deeply gratified by your kind letter. Your high-minded will to pursue world peace and the economic recovery of all nations is unprecedented. The French government shares the same spirit and holds the same goals. Your esteemed letter will be carefully studied." (Havas, 17th)

(Paris) Our correspondent called on Premier Daladier and asked for his opinion on President Roosevelt's declaration. The Premier replied that he was sincerely pleased with President Roosevelt's declaration, and that its noble ideas should be admired by all the French people. If the directions indicated in this declaration can be followed, the World Economic Conference and the Disarmament Conference can definitely be expected to succeed. France and the United States are jointly maintaining peace in an effective manner, and this is another cause for celebration. Daladier also said that Roosevelt's work benefits all mankind, and he is extremely willing to assist in his efforts and wishes him success. (Havas, 17th)

(Paris) The leader of the Radical Socialist Party (i.e., the current ruling party), Chairman of the Chamber of Deputies Foreign Affairs Committee, and former Prime Minister Herriot, attended the Foreign Affairs Committee meeting and described his visit to Washington. He repeatedly expressed his gratitude for the warm reception from President Roosevelt and other important American figures. Herriot then casually mentioned Roosevelt's declaration, saying that it contained two key points: (1) The U.S. government intends to participate in European affairs in a more active and direct manner; (2) The U.S. government clearly opposes any German attempt to rearm. (Havas, 17th)

French Press Commentary is Mixed 31

(Paris) Although French newspapers have mixed opinions on the U.S. President's announcement to the world's forty-four nations regarding disarmament and foreign policy, French Premier Daladier has issued a statement declaring that the U.S. President's statement has given him the most sincere satisfaction. He says that the main theme of the U.S. President's statement will help the success of the economic and disarmament conferences. The U.S. and France are now also jointly undertaking effective actions for the maintenance of peace. (Reuters, 17th)

(Paris) The French national morning newspapers have all adopted an extremely calm and cautious attitude towards President Roosevelt's announced disarmament plan. The extreme right-wing newspapers have even resolutely expressed their rejection of it. The greatest causes of this negative attitude are probably (1) Roosevelt did not mention the war debt issue; (2) The declaration did not provide France with sufficient guarantees to avoid foreign aggression; (3) The declaration did not propose appropriate measures to restrain aggressor nations. Therefore, the famous French jurist Mr. Barthelemy wrote an article in the Journal de Paris, stating that the most important part of Roosevelt's declaration is Roosevelt's declaration that the United States is willing to cooperate with other countries to punish countries that disrupt peace. Unfortunately, President Roosevelt did not provide a more detailed explanation of how the United States would cooperate with other countries. Mr. Barthelemy further stated that Roosevelt's declaration did not mention sanctions at all, or perhaps the U.S. President did not want to place this heavy responsibility on the Senate. In fact, France cannot but first demand the greatest possible reduction in armaments before it can feel secure. Mr. Potin of the Echo de Paris rashly refuted the U.S. disarmament plan, claiming that U.S. policy is an ignorant, unthinking guideline. Even if aggressive armaments can be abolished, war can still occur at any time, because the greatest problem today is that treaties are no longer respected and can be arbitrarily torn up. The French army is the greatest force for maintaining existing treaties. If it has to be reduced due to the disarmament conference, then the treaties will be destroyed even more quickly. (Reuters, 17th)

U.S. Diplomacy Abandons Isolation 32

Geneva Praises Roosevelt's Courage

(Geneva) League of Nations figures favorably comment on U.S. President Roosevelt's letter to the heads of state of 54 nations, all believing it to be a serious warning to Germany, hoping that Hitler will retreat and save face. German figures here alone express dissatisfaction, especially regarding the section of President Roosevelt's declaration opposing German rearmament. American figures say that President Roosevelt is the first U.S. President in history to make such a clear declaration. The Journal de Genève reports that since the European War, the United States has always been isolated. Roosevelt's declaration this time can be said to be a sign that the United States has begun to abandon its isolationist policy. In terms of world peace, this alone can be considered a courageous expression. (Havas, 17th)

China's Turmoil is an Inevitable Stage of the Transitional Process

Reforms Currently Implemented are Elaborately Managed with Rapid Progress

Minister Sung's Attendance at the London Economic Conference May Not Be Prolonged

(Washington) T.V. Soong today issued an appeal to America, asking for tolerance regarding China's turmoil. It must be understood that the transition from autocracy to democracy is a gradual process. Allowing each person the right to speak in the process, so that the democratic system can achieve greatness, will inevitably make this process more stable, but also more gradual than under the guidance of an emperor. Therefore, it will take longer for China to achieve its goals, but China would rather spend more time developing from within, becoming a truly large organization, than merely pursuing superficial, mechanical civilization of the new era and the power of new armaments, without seeking spiritual enrichment and the realization of concepts of justice and fairness. The reforms that China is implementing are quite elaborately managed, but these reforms are now progressing quite rapidly. This is an important fact. Last year, China balanced its budget. In these difficult times, and still needing to continue raising funds to resist Japanese aggression, it is able to achieve this result, which is worthy of pride. (Reuters, 17th)

The Qinghai-Tibet Agreement Has Not Yet Been Signed

The Xinjiang Incident Can Be Resolved Soon

(Nanjing) Ma Shi Meng, the secretary of the newly organized 9th Division of Qinghai Province, escorted students from Qinghai Province who were recommended to the Central Military Academy to Beijing. Last year, Tibetan troops invaded Qinghai, but were repelled by teams dispatched by Ma Bufang's division. Qinghai Province sent Ma Xun as its representative to begin negotiations, but no agreement has been signed yet. Ma Tengyun will come to Beijing at the end of this month to report to the Central Government on the Qinghai-Tibet peace talks. He left Qinghai shortly after the Xinjiang incident, so he does not know the situation well afterward. The reasons for the Hui people's opposition to the provincial government in this incident are (1) Jin Shuren's maladministration in Xinjiang; (2) The collection of exorbitant taxes and levies, which the people cannot bear; (3) The recruitment of White Russian troops and the arrest of local Hui people. All the ethnic groups in the new province could not bear Jin's oppression and rose up in opposition. Now, he has requested to resign, which has been approved and he has left the province. This matter can be resolved soon. After the Central Government sends Pacification Commissioner Huang Musong to offer comfort, this matter will be easier to resolve. (Special Dispatch, 18th)

Japanese Foreign Ministry and Army Ministry Agree

Puppet Organization Buys the Chinese Eastern Railway 45

(Tokyo) It is heard that the Foreign Ministry and the Army Ministry have reached an agreement on the "Manchukuo" purchase of the Chinese Eastern Railway. The Foreign Ministry held an important meeting today, attended by representatives from the Foreign and Army Ministries and Mr. Ohashi, the Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs of "Manchukuo." According to newspaper reports, the discussion was about the valuation of the Chinese Eastern Railway and the method of payment. It is heard that Japan and Manchukuo agree that the Soviet Union is sincere in selling this railway, so it should be purchased to eliminate the source of future conflicts. (Reuters, 18th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Army's opinion on the issue of purchasing the Eastern Railway was formally submitted to the Foreign Ministry on the 18th. They frankly stated that the purchase should be made by "Manchukuo." As for the specific issues, they will be decided in the future through negotiations between Ohashi, the "Manchukuo" Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, and the relevant parties. However, "Manchukuo" has previously taken the position of not recognizing the Soviet Union's ownership of the Eastern Railway, so it seems that a meeting will be convened among the Foreign Ministry, Army Ministry, Finance Ministry, Colonial Ministry, Kwantung Army, and South Manchuria Railway to resolve the negotiations. (Dentsu, 18th)

(Tokyo) "Manchukuo" Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Ohashi visited Director-General Tani of the Asian Affairs Bureau of the Foreign Ministry at 11:00 a.m. today to discuss the Eastern Railway and other issues. As a result, even if the "Manchukuo" purchases the Chinese Eastern Railway, the Soviet Union seems to have no objection, so it is beneficial for the "Manchukuo" to conduct purchase negotiations and to open a joint committee among Japan, Russia, and Manchukuo, so efforts are being made to realize this. The committee will be located in Harbin, etc. A consensus was reached, and the purchase price, purchase date, and methods will be decided through further negotiations. (Dentsu, 18th)

(Tokyo Correspondence) Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov has formally proposed the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway to Japan. The Japanese government considers this issue to be important and is now carefully studying it. The most important points of this issue are the price and method of payment. The Japanese and Russian authorities have not yet formally expressed any opinions. However, the Russian side insists that the selling price is 300 million gold rubles. The Japanese side intends to purchase it for 80 million yuan because of the recent political and economic significance of the railway. There is now a large discrepancy between the claims of the two sides. As for the method of payment, the Japanese side is considering three options: (1) Transform the Chinese Eastern Railway into a joint-stock organization, with the Soviet Union owning its shares; (2) Pay part of the purchase price with long-term checks; (3) Pay part of the purchase price in cash.

French Ambassador to Japan Martell visited Vice Minister Arita of the Foreign Ministry at noon on the 8th of this month to inquire whether the Soviet Union's proposal to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway to Japan was true. France is concerned about this issue because of its debt relationship with Russian banks. The French Ambassador also heard the Japanese government's attitude and policy regarding the establishment of a joint committee of Russia, Japan, and "Manchukuo." Vice Minister Arita replied that Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov did indeed propose the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. As for the issue of establishing a joint committee of the three countries, Japan hopes that it will be established as soon as possible. It is heard that the French Ambassador argued that France has a major interest in the Chinese Eastern Railway for the following reasons: During the Russian imperial era, when the Chinese Eastern Railway was built, it was intended to sign a "Contract on the Construction and Operation of the Chinese Eastern Railway" with the Qing government. However, because it was rejected by the Qing government, the Russian-Chinese Bank of the Russian government was the nominal party involved. On February 10, 1895, it invested a principal of 6 million rubles to build the Chinese Eastern Railway, and this principal was provided by a banking syndicate in Paris at that time. Since then, the French government has claimed to have an interest in the Chinese Eastern Railway whenever problems have occurred. However, of the 6 million rubles of the Russian-Chinese Bank, only 5 million rubles were paid. The Chinese Eastern Railway later issued its own bonds and raised a huge sum of 350 million rubles. According to Japanese observations, because the Chinese Eastern Railway did not borrow money like ordinary railways, it was not collateral for the bank. Therefore, France has no legal basis to interfere in the sales negotiations between Japan and the Soviet Union. (Japan United News Agency)

Hitler's Speech Has a Positive Impact

Disarmament Situation Greatly Clarified 46

European and American Countries Feel Relieved

Disarmament Conference to Reconvene Today

Obstacles to the Four-Power Pact Also Cleared

(Berlin) After Chancellor Hitler's speech, the German Parliament passed a resolution declaring that the Parliament, considering the equality issue to be vital to Germany's life, is willing to unanimously support the government in this matter. This proves the enthusiasm of the German people for supporting Hitler's claim to equality. Berlin and the whole country regard Hitler's speech as a peace message to the world, because it explains that Germany has no aggressive intentions, does not want to forcibly demand the revision of borders, and if other countries are willing to do what Germany is doing, then Germany is prepared to implement disarmament. (Reuters, 17th)

(Washington) According to White House sources, President Roosevelt felt happy after listening to German Chancellor Hitler's broadcast speech, because Hitler supported his movement to seek peace. The White House expressed the opinion that there is now a good reason to be optimistic that President Roosevelt's advocacy of banning aggressive actions will be successful. The U.S. President's proposal to abolish offensive weapons and his endorsement of the principles of the British Prime Minister's disarmament plan have been endorsed by the German Chancellor. The State Department attaches great importance to this point. The German Chancellor's tone can be regarded as moderate and exciting. These are all good signs for Geneva. The State Department considers it most important that Hitler said that Germany wants other countries to disarm, not to rearm itself. This shows that Germany wants to seek some revisions to the Treaty of Versailles by peaceful means, not by violence. As for the German Chancellor's warning that if other countries exert unequal pressure on Germany, then Germany will be forced to withdraw from the League of Nations, it is widely believed that the general moderate attitude expressed in Hitler's speech will prevent the situation from reaching a breaking point. (Reuters, 17th)

(London) German Chancellor Hitler's speech has generally made a good impression. Political circles in Paris acknowledge that his tone is moderate and say that Hitler is clearly trying to please President Roosevelt, MacDonald, and Mussolini. People in Paris believe that Hitler has realized Roosevelt's hints, so he is willing to turn scolding into euphemism. However, the gap between France and Germany regarding disarmament remains as wide as before. (Reuters, 17th)

(Paris) When the German Reichstag voted to support Hitler's speech, the members of the Democratic Socialist faction of the Reichstag also participated. In the French Chamber of Deputies lounge today, commenting on this matter, Socialist leader Blum declared to our correspondent as follows: "I can explain two things to you regarding this matter. First, there were a limited number of Democratic Socialist deputies participating in the Reichstag meeting this time. Second, the deputies' participation in the vote was contrary to the party's wishes and contrary to the instructions of the party's leadership to the party's representatives in various Berlin councils." Blum also made a statement about the possible consequences of the German Democratic Socialist deputies' participation in the vote, saying, "I can only explain my opinion with extreme reservation on this matter. However, there are differing opinions among the leaders and a large part of the members of the German Democratic Socialist Party. In fact, it can be said to be equal to a split." When the reporter asked about the opinion of the French Socialist Party on this matter, Blum replied, "Our feelings are well known. We believe that the only way to deal with Hitler's dictatorship is to fight to the end. Some members of the Socialist Party believe that a compromise should be adopted towards Hitler's politics, or a passive attitude of endurance should be adopted. We should not cooperate with such party members."

(Paris) According to inquiries made by our representative with the competent authorities, although people generally hold a reserved attitude towards the speech delivered by German Chancellor Hitler yesterday, they do not hold malicious intent. People are particularly concerned about two things: one is the section of Hitler's speech that does not advocate the use of force, and the other is Hitler's permission that Germany will never deliberately destroy the current treaties. Also, judging from the tone of certain sections of Hitler's speech, it seems that Hitler has already changed his policy and admits that some of the methods in his policy are inappropriate. Rome The people of Rome all welcome Hitler's speech, calling it a moderate and reasonable article. His willingness to accept Mussolini's proposed Four-Power Pact and his willingness to sign mutual non-aggression agreements can all dispel rumors that Germany has aggressive intentions toward its eastern borders. The German Embassy has recently been in contact with the Foreign Ministry. Non-political circles believe that the moderation of Hitler's speech may be due to this reason. In short, it is generally felt that the obstacles to Mussolini's Four-Power Pact have now been cleared and its realization is expected. (Reuters, 17th)

(London) The London Times commented today on German Chancellor Hitler's speech in parliament yesterday, saying that the world can see a glimpse of Hitler's political skills in his speech. Other British newspapers also have this view, all believing that Hitler's speech is moderate and sincere, creating a better atmosphere. The British government feels that the world's attention is now focused on Geneva, which will have real progress because of Hitler's speech. The London financial market has also reduced its turmoil because of Hitler's speech. At the same time, prices in the market rose, although there was no shortage of profit-taking, and the close was finally stable. (Reuters, 18th)

Definition of "Aggressor Nation" Determined 47

(Geneva) After German Chancellor Hitler guaranteed that Germany would not forcibly violate existing treaties and declared his willingness to support a non-aggression pact, Geneva was relieved today. Although the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference will extend its meeting to Friday to study Hitler's speech, the Security Committee, at its final meeting, adopted the Soviet Union's definition of an aggressor nation. The content is largely consistent with the US President's policy of not sending troops abroad, summarized as follows:

(1) Nations that declare war on other countries

(2) Nations that invade the territory of other countries without declaring war

(3) Nations that blockade other countries by sea

(4) Nations that bomb the territory of neighboring countries in any way

(5) Nations that send troops to land or station land, naval, or air forces in the territory of other countries

Paris reports that the French were greatly relieved to hear that Hitler's speech was not as激烈 as expected. US Representative Davis will soon elaborate on the US President's proposals at the Disarmament Conference and declare that the United States is willing to sign a consultation pact and support the supervision of armaments. (Seventeenth National Telegram)

(Geneva) Hitler's speech has aroused a generally favorable impression here, considered skillfully worded, especially moving to the Anglo-Saxon nations. Many believe that Hitler has shown that he is worthy of being a politician, but Geneva disarmament experts have given it extremely harsh criticism, saying that the German Chancellor's words are not much different from the theory held by the German representative to the Disarmament Conference, Nadolny. The General Commission of the Disarmament Conference was originally scheduled to meet on Thursday, but now it has been changed to Friday afternoon, when German representative Nadolny and French representative Paul-Boncour will both be able to arrive here. (Seventeenth Reuters Telegram)

(Berlin) Since the publication of Chancellor Hitler's speech in the Reichstag, various Berlin newspapers have published lengthy reports and unanimous commentaries in support. However, it is absolutely necessary that equal organizations in all countries should also be subject to international joint management in this way. The newspaper stated that this kind of concession is more important than lengthy verbal debates and can dispel the years-long rumors of secret German plans, like clearing away clouds and seeing the light of day. 明令褒揚王瑚 48

(Nanjing) On the 18th, the National Government issued an order stating that Wang Hu, the former Deputy Chairman of the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission and member of the Relief Committee, was loyal, honest, and incorruptible. He had long been known for his good reputation in civil administration. In recent years, he had been dedicated to disaster relief and investigation, tirelessly making plans. News of his sudden passing is deeply mourned. Wang Hu should be specially commended, and the Examination Yuan should instruct the ministry to grant generous compensation to highlight his hard work and encourage integrity. Supreme Court Judgment

Case of Traitor Hu Lifu 52

Appeal Rejected, Hu Sentenced to Death

(Nanjing) In the case of the traitor Hu Lifu, the Jiangsu High Court sentenced him to life imprisonment. The prosecutor of the court disagreed with the verdict and filed an appeal. The Supreme Court has recently issued a judgment, of which the main text, facts, and reasons are excerpted as follows: (Main text) The original judgment regarding the crime of serving in the enemy army and the execution of the sentence are both revoked. Hu Lifu is sentenced to death for serving in the enemy army, and deprived of his civil rights indefinitely. Combined with the sentences imposed by the original judgment for the crimes of intending to profit by providing gambling venues, selling opium, and intending to profit by providing opium dens in hostels, the death penalty is executed, and civil rights are deprived indefinitely. The rest of the appeal is rejected. (Facts) After the January 28th Incident, when the Japanese army was causing trouble in Shanghai, and our 19th Route Army retreated to the second line of defense, Zhabei was occupied by the Japanese army. Hu was introduced by Japanese person Washizaki to the 4th Unit of the Japanese army. Initially, translators and others from the four battalions formed the Jiangbei Command. After it was disbanded, Washizaki introduced Hu Lifu. Then, the commander-in-chief of the Japanese army, Sawamatsu, and the commander of the 4th Battalion, Yamashita, ordered Hu to organize the Beishi Local Citizens Maintenance Association to replace the Jiangbei Command, and Hu was appointed as the chairman. The association was divided into six groups: general affairs, finance, patrol officers, investigation, transportation, and sanitation. There was also a social group. The association had about four to five hundred people. The association's affairs were handled in accordance with the wishes of the 4th Battalion of the Japanese army. All residents moving out of Zhabei were assessed a fee of 2% of the value of their goods, and Hu issued exit permits, which the Japanese army checked and released. In ten days, more than 3,000 yuan was extorted. Japanese soldiers often came to inspect and Yamashita praised Hu. The maintenance was very good. Later, after the League of Nations inquired with the Japanese consulate, it was canceled. Therefore, after the cancellation, the Jiuhe Company was organized to open gambling houses, opium dens, and sell opium, which was still presided over by Hu. Two weeks later, more than 9,000 yuan was collected again. When the Japanese army withdrew from Zhabei, Hu, fearing punishment, hid in Washizaki's home. He was repeatedly ordered to be arrested but was not found. It was not until September 16th that Hu was arrested by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau and sent to the prosecutor of the Jiangsu High Court for investigation and prosecution. (Reasons) This case is divided into two parts: (1) Regarding the organization of the Maintenance Association, Hu confessed to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, "Washizaki called me out, and also said that the Japanese headquarters wanted me to organize the Beishi Local Citizens Maintenance Association. I am the chairman." He also said, "There are plainclothes patrol officers to maintain local order." He also said, "We cannot violate the comrades of the 4th Battalion in our work." The collection of freight handling fees was entirely handled by me. The appellant has already confessed in detail how he entrusted Washizaki to dredge up the organization of the Beishi Local Citizens Maintenance Association to replace the Jiangbei Command, how he was commissioned by the Japanese army, was inspected by them, how he divided into groups to handle affairs and added female inspectors and police detectives, how he inherited the Jiangbei Command's methods, and levied freight handling taxes. How he maintained the rear for the Japanese army when it was unable to maintain public order. How he handled affairs in accordance with the wishes of the 4th Battalion of the Japanese army. All these things have been confessed without denial. This is consistent with the investigation report obtained by the Shanghai Municipal Government. As for the appellant's defense that the purpose of organizing the association was to handle charitable matters, and provide proof, based on various facts, it is difficult to conceal that he was commissioned by the Japanese army. In addition, the appellant also argued that he did not serve in the enemy army and had no behavior that endangered the Republic of China. The appellant was commissioned by the Japanese army and openly organized an illegal organization to maintain order in the rear for the enemy, which increased the danger of the national army resisting the enemy. If this is not called serving, what is serving? If this is not called endangering the Republic of China, what is endangering? The above situation is really unforgivable. The prosecutor said that the original sentence of only life imprisonment was too lenient, and it is hard to say that there is no reason. (2) Regarding the organization of the command, Hu confessed, "After we retreated to Linping Road on April 11, I wanted to organize the Jiuhe Company to open businesses such as buying and selling opium and tobacco, and I was responsible for it. After two weeks, a total of more than 9,000 yuan was collected." The appellant has already confessed the details in detail, which is consistent with the investigation report obtained by the Shanghai Municipal Government. There is nothing inappropriate in the rules of evidence adopted in the various crimes sentenced by the original judgment. The appellant's grounds for appeal are still untenable. Based on the above arguments, in accordance with Article 409, Paragraph 1, Article 410, Paragraph 1, Section 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Article 42, Article 109, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, Article 6, Article 10 of the Emergency Crime Punishment Law for Endangering the Nation, Article 74, Article 120, Article 57, Paragraph 3, Article 70, Section 1 of the Criminal Law, and Article 408, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the judgment is made as in the main text. (Eighteenth Central News Agency Telegram)

Zheng Yanfen Talks

International Convention on Limiting Narcotic Drugs 66

(Nanjing) The Chairman of the League of Nations Opium Advisory Committee in Geneva made an important statement regarding the 1931 Convention for Limiting the Manufacture and Regulating the Distribution of Narcotic Drugs. It is also reported that the convention is scheduled to take effect on July 9th. A reporter interviewed Mr. Zheng Yanfen, Secretary of the League of Nations, who stated: (1) According to known statistics, the production of morphine in major countries has increased from 30 tons to 59 tons, an increase of approximately 50%. Of the 266 tons of morphine produced by various countries, at least 72 tons have flowed into private sales. Therefore, the convention was established. This convention represents significant progress compared to the Hague Convention and the Geneva Convention. The purpose of this convention is to strictly investigate the distribution of narcotic drugs and directly limit production. (2) The 1931 Convention has five advantages over previous conventions: (1) The scope of restrictions is broader and more clearly defined than before. (2) The total annual production worldwide is not freely determined by the manufacturing countries but is decided based on the prior estimates of the consuming countries. (3) Each contracting manufacturing country should compile statistics annually and send them to Geneva for review by the four Central Supervisory Committees, which will assess the estimates of the legitimate necessary quantity of a certain narcotic drug. (4) The articles on prohibition restrictions and acceptance are more stringent and practical than before. (3) From a legal and economic perspective, this convention has special provisions for industrial and commercial issues. Not only do the contracting countries have obligations to fulfill, but non-contracting countries can also impose restrictions. This convention represents the first attempt to control the narcotic drug industry with the power of nations and international organizations. The contracting countries authorize international organizations to determine production volume based on the estimates of each country and to supervise distribution and consumption. This is unprecedented in economic history. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

Cooperation with the National Economic Commission 67

US Airship

Accident Investigation Report 89

Caused by Poor Piloting

▲ National News Agency, Washington, 17th: The report on the investigation of the Akron airship accident was released today. According to the report, the cause of the accident was due to errors in judgment and incorrect commands. No defects were found. The ship's commander, McCracken, had poor orientation, causing the airship to enter the center of the storm, where it was blown down by strong downdrafts. However, the incompleteness of the weather map made accurate judgment difficult. Furthermore, McCracken's order to change direction by 15 degrees was misunderstood as 50 degrees, which led the airship into the lightning that it had been trying to avoid, also contributing to the accident. Senators now believe that the report does not address many issues of particular concern to the Senate and may form another committee to investigate the case before the recess. Today, several senators pointed out that the commander of the battle fleet forced the best aviation experts to depart with the fleet, leaving less experienced individuals in charge of the airship, which was the fundamental cause of the accident. It is said that if Lieutenant Colonel Rosenthal had commanded the ship, such an error in judgment would not have occurred.

The War Has Abated

New Developments in the Northern Situation (Reaching) 91

Huang Fu Comes to Beiping to Preside, Tianjin and Beiping May Be Safe for Now

Japanese Military Aims Focused on Completing Manchuria-Mongolia Policy

Special Dispatch from Beiping: Although the Japanese military's large-scale invasion this time involves an extreme conspiracy, its main purpose remains to ensure the occupation of the three northeastern provinces and Rehe-Chahar, and to complete its Manchuria-Mongolia policy. If it can gain a considerable grasp on its main objectives, then it can temporarily satisfy its demands and no longer advance endlessly. Recently, in the first step of its plan, the eastern route occupied Luanzhou and Fengrun, important towns, and the northern route occupied the key passes of Shixia and Miyun, taking dangerous positions to threaten Beiping and Tianjin. This has largely satisfied its wishes and can be considered a small conclusion to the military action, temporarily waiting for changes in the situation to determine its future course of action. Since the frontline became tense and Beiping and Tianjin were in danger, we have considered Beiping and Tianjin as the lifeline of the north, of utmost importance. If there are any oversights, the whole country will be shaken. It is imperative to use all efforts to ensure their safety. In addition to deploying large forces to make preparations for combat and defense, practical and appropriate measures are also being taken. Jiang Bocheng, a member of the Standing Committee of the Military Council, went to Tianjin the day before yesterday to meet with important figures in Tianjin to discuss matters. At the same time, important generals from the front have also been ordered to come to Beiping to discuss everything in detail. The security of Beiping and Tianjin can be assured for the time being. Huang Fu, the newly appointed Chairman of the Administrative Yuan's Resident Beiping Political Affairs Committee, has discussed relevant measures for northern political affairs with key figures in the central government in Nanjing and Shanghai, and will come to Beiping to preside. The northern situation is likely to have new developments. Several days ago, a Japanese man named Nagai indicated to a certain party that the Japanese military's current rapid occupation of Beiping and Tianjin has small benefits but large targets, which is not cost-effective. Chahar has an extremely large relationship with Manchuria and Mongolia, and it is imperative to take it, and so on. The Japanese are extremely cunning, and it is questionable whether this statement is credible, but based on a general assessment, it is likely not far from the truth. Mutō, the Commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army, issued a statement yesterday, stating that the Japanese military's objectives have been achieved and that if the Chinese army abandons its challenging attitude, it will withdraw. This statement is very smooth, and it seems to be issued for a reason. In the near future, a live drama of withdrawing troops from Luan East may be staged again. Since yesterday (the 15th), the war on the front lines has abated. Although the enemy occupying Shixia continues to attack our new positions in the Jiusongling area, its momentum has been greatly reduced compared to the past few days. This morning (the 16th), the Japanese military did not take any active actions and has sent Mongolian puppet troops to build solid defensive fortifications and set up electric wire nets within its positions, seemingly intending to switch from offense to defense. Several Japanese aircraft continue to scout and bomb Miyun, but their intensity is not as fierce as in the previous two days. On the eastern route, the situation in Tangshan was once chaotic, with passenger trains only running to Lutai. The phone lines to Fengrun are still down, and the situation is unclear. The majority of our army is concentrated in the Lutai and Yutian areas. There were no fierce battles between the two sides last night and this morning. Precautions in Beiping and Tianjin are still very strict to prevent criminals from taking advantage of the situation, but the morale of the people has been much calmer than in the previous two days. (16th)

× × × ×

Enemy Re-Attacks the Central Eastern Line Situation 92

By Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

Special Telegram from Xu Ge Zhuang: Military secrets, rapid shifts, distant rumors, difficult to discern the truth. Even close-range interviews are hard to immediately publish. However, facts are facts, shifts are shifts. The advance, retreat, victory, and defeat of the war are facts and cannot be hidden forever. This time, the enemy is once again launching a large-scale attack south of our Great Wall line, attempting to encircle Tianjin and Beijing, and sweep across North China. The situation is extremely clear. Here, I will continue from my previous dispatch and briefly describe the war situation on the eastern front, based on my personal observations. Since the enemy launched its attack on the 7th, its main force has been advancing westward along the Pingyu Highway. The defending troops of He's unit, stationed on the Kailuan section of the railway which runs almost parallel to the highway, have also been affected. This is a vicious tactic adopted by the Japanese army. However, if our railway line defending troops can maintain a spirit of sacrifice, and resolutely defend the strong fortifications already built at key locations west of Luan and in the Kailuan section, the enemy forces advancing westward along the Pingyu Highway will inevitably have concerns about their flanks and rear. They can then genuinely link up with Wang Yizhe's troops, who are desperately resisting the brutal enemy on that highway, and support each other, seize opportunities to adopt pincer or flanking tactics, constantly send strong cavalry to harass the enemy's flanks and rear, and let armored vehicles continue to operate as guerrillas along the railway line, to fulfill their responsibility of liaison, cover, and emergency response. Even if they cannot achieve a major victory, they can still slightly blunt the enemy's momentum, making it difficult for them to fulfill their ambition of quickly capturing the towns and villages they have invaded, even if they pay the highest price. At the same time, Wang's and Weng Zhang's divisions will not have to solely face strong enemies and endure intense sacrifices, to the point where they cannot even get a moment to regroup and reorganize after each intense battle. This kind of war situation can be discerned from the accounts of wounded soldiers from Wang's unit encountered at various stations, crawling their way here, or from the words of fleeing soldiers lingering and waiting to be taken in. Currently, the enemy forces are still divided into two routes: one is fiercely attacking westward towards Wangguanying in Hazelnut Town, east of Fengrun County. In the past two days, enemy planes have already flown to Fengrun City to drop bombs. The county magistrate, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, and wealthy merchants have all fled to Xugezhuang and are living in a school. It is said that there are still more than 200 members of the defense corps in the city, cooperating with the army to maintain order. The other route is following and pursuing our retreating army along the Beining Road, probably because of international relations, and because they know that the defending troops on that road will inevitably be drawn back by the advance of the enemy forces on the left flank, so the troops they have sent are mostly puppet troops, not the main force. Our army retreated from Luancheng and other stations, villages, and towns, and the enemy only dared to invade the next day or the day after. On the night of the 12th, the reporter retreated with the army from Luancheng to Guye. At 2 PM on the 13th, I heard the order to immediately transport heavy materials to the rear. At 8 PM, just as I was about to go to bed, I heard the order to retreat to Xugezhuang immediately. In two nights and one day, the retreat route was nearly 200 li. The refugees along the way, who were following the army's advance and retreat, suddenly panicked like startled cranes, and were as chaotic as ants in a hot pot, not knowing what to do. People eagerly vying to get on the westward-bound trains rubbed shoulders and were extremely crowded. The cries of children and the rattling of carts echoed endlessly, and it was even more difficult for women who needed to relieve themselves to do so than climbing to heaven. Only then did I realize that the refugees were mostly middle-class or lower-class families. Those above the middle class had already fled to Tianjin and Beijing after the fall of Yuguan, leaving hardly anyone behind. This is no exaggeration. At the Zhang family in Xugezhuang, where the Central Propaganda Team was staying, plaques inscribed with "Eager for Public Good" and "Respectful of the Hometown" erected in the second year of the Xuantong reign were hung in the front hall. The floors were inlaid with tiles, and the walls were painted, the building was magnificent, no less than the wealthy in the city. However, because the family had taken their family far away to avoid the disaster of war, the carved windows of their halls were mostly nests for crows and sparrows. The chirping of the chicks was within reach, the desolate state was lamentable. The village had a market day yesterday, every five days, and the buying and selling of goods was mostly pig bristles, the whole city smelled strangely. Next were grains and groceries. The grains in eastern Luan were mostly insufficient for local production, and in previous years, they relied entirely on the northeast for adjustment. Now they rely on Shanxi. The transaction of this season's seeds is extremely cold. The spring planting has already been missed, and the autumn harvest will be even more hopeless. At about 11 AM, when the main street was bustling with people, three enemy planes suddenly flew in, rumbling. They reconnoitered for a week, and then flew away. But the city's merchants have dispersed in an uproar, and the refugees waiting for the train at the station were even more trembling and had nowhere to hide. This plane was flying from the northeast along the railway line to reconnoiter at various stations. In Tangshan, it dropped two bombs, which slightly damaged our supply vehicles. Soon, ten newly built locomotives and countless important machines were transported from Tangshan, along with more than ten baggage cars, full of ammunition and flour. A soldier tried to board, but was scolded by the train's guard, saying that it was an ammunition car, and even if he had a pass, it would be difficult to go along. The soldier was not convinced, and the two sides argued, even drawing their knives at each other. Later, an officer saw it, fired a shot to scare them away. On a wounded soldier's car, there were several civilians, also covered in blood, groaning incessantly. I went over and talked to them, and they replied that they were from a village in Ninghe, and they were hired by the local area to follow the carts to the front. The conditions were that those who had money would contribute money, and those who did not would contribute labor. The employer would first give them ten yuan for living expenses, and they would agree that if they returned home safely within a month, the cart and horse would be divided equally. If they returned home after a month, they would enjoy all the benefits. If they unfortunately encountered an accident, it would be regarded as a national service. The convoy consisted of more than 30 carts. A few days ago, they were transporting them to the Shaheyi·Laoyemiao area. Suddenly, three enemy planes attacked, dropping bombs one after another, the sky and earth were shaking. The carts and vehicles were all bombed and destroyed. Those who barely survived also had little hope of being cured. At that time, a certain battalion of Weng's division also encountered a battle in front, unprepared, and retreated in a hurry, the situation was even more tragic. Under the willows at the station, there were several suitcases piled up, and two young women were sitting there, dressed fashionably, talking to each other. They said, "The special train fleeing from the Shanhaiguan Incident was full of officers' wives. Later, they learned from the telephone that the situation had returned to peace, and they returned to Changli. This time, our regimental commander (the younger one said) was originally defending the area east of the Luanhe Railway Bridge. He once said that if the railway bridge was bombed by the enemy, how would we cross the river? But in fact, it was not the case. Now the entire division has safely arrived at Leizhuang." The older one said, "If you are an officer to the rank of regimental commander, it is easy to be safe and promoted. The wife is really lucky." She smiled and said, "It's really annoying. What luck is there? Just like last night, the regimental commander was already tired and asleep, but the phone kept ringing. Sometimes I really couldn't bear to answer it. Zhang Xueliang has resigned, and there are still two months of salary that have not been paid. Recently, I heard that the authorities will set the salaries of military agency staff, starting from June. Generals will get 50% of 800 yuan, lieutenant generals will get 60% of 500 yuan, major generals will get 70% of 300 yuan, colonels will get 80% of 240 yuan, lieutenant colonels will get 90% of 170 yuan, majors will get 135 yuan, almost nothing. Captains will get 100%. There are so many tricks. Not to mention slightly reducing the percentage, I am only afraid that it will not be paid, then what will happen?" The reporter was very surprised, so he found a way to find out from her orderly that she was the second wife of the regimental commander of the 9th Brigade □□□ Regiment. The other, who considered herself inferior, was the wife of the director of a veterinary hospital. Both had to temporarily leave their husbands and go to Beiping first because of the tense situation. After a while, the delayed passenger train arrived, and they all rushed to board the train. The reporter also silently recited the slogans posted on the willows along the way: "Farmers should intensify cultivation to increase food," "The whole country should unite to mobilize and support the central government to resist the brutal Japanese," "Support Chairman Chiang, who is painstakingly responsible for resisting Japan and saving the country," "Do you know that ten Korean families share a kitchen knife? Do you know that the Japanese are confiscating civilian guns in the three northeastern provinces? Then you will understand the pain after the country is subjugated." He slowly walked out of the station and suddenly encountered Zhao and Wang from Northeast University, who came to participate in the anti-Japanese work, but because they were not approved by the authorities, they could not solve the food problem, so they had to take the train back to Ping in disappointment. Li, a student from Xiamen University, and Shi, a student from Yanjing University, who were working here as propagandists, were quite determined and had experienced many hardships. However, the food problem was also a constant problem. I record this to tell patriotic youths who want to come to serve that they should have proper contact in advance. (May 16)

Huang Fu Passes Through Jinan on His Way North 93

(Meeting with Han Fuju and Making a Statement)

Jinan Correspondence: At a time when the central government is preoccupied with the tense war situation at the front, it has established the North China Political Reorganization Committee, with Huang Fu as the chairman. After receiving the order, Huang exchanged views with various important figures in Shanghai on the reorganization of North China's politics. Recently, due to repeated telegrams from all sectors of Tianjin and Beijing urging him to come north, he took the Jinjing train from Shanghai to Beijing yesterday morning to pay respects to President Wang and ask for instructions. That night, he took the Pingpu train 202 north with He Qigong, Secretary-General of the Political Committee, and his entourage, He Jiecai, etc. Qiu Wei, Chairman of the Jinpu Railway Committee, specially reserved two cars for Huang. Qiu also planned to come north with Huang, but got off the train and returned to Beijing at the Citibank camp in Pukou due to some business. Because Huang was passing through Jinan midway, he had business to discuss with Han Fuju, Chairman of the Provincial Government. He had sent a telegram to Han in advance, so Han and Zhang Weicun, the Provincial Committee member, Wang Fangting, the Director of the Department of Industry, and Chai Dongsheng, the Director of the Salt Affairs Tax Police Bureau, all came to the station to welcome him. It is said that Huang served as Minister of Foreign Affairs in the 17th year of the Republic. He came to Jinan once during the May 3rd Massacre. This time, he passed through Jinan again, just as the war in western Luan was tense, and the situation in Tianjin and Beijing was critical. One could not help but feel emotional. The train arrived in Jinan at 6 PM. After the train stopped, Han boarded the train to meet with Huang. Then Han, Huang, He Qigong, and others got off the train together.

Talking to Reporters 94

The reporter interviewed Huang at the station and made the following remarks. The reporter asked, "What is the chairman's mission this time?" Huang replied with a smile, "To reorganize North China's political affairs." The reporter asked, "At this critical time in North China, what good strategies does the chairman have to save the situation?" Huang replied, "This is not a simple question. Everyone must deliberate at length before a decision can be made." The reporter asked, "When can the North China Political Committee be formally established?" Huang replied, "There are more than 20 members of the Political Committee, who are still scattered in various places. Although I am responsible for reorganizing North China's political affairs, I must wait until all the members have arrived before I can plan and proceed." After the conversation, Han Fuju, Huang Fu, and He Qigong took a car to the provincial government together, and the welcoming staff also followed. After arriving at the provincial government, they had a lively discussion on everything in Han's office.

Answering Three Questions 95

The reporter visited Huang again at the provincial government, and Huang sent his secretary, He Jiecai, to meet with the reporter on his behalf. The reporter asked three questions, which He answered on behalf of the reporter as follows: (1) "At this critical time in North China, does the central government have any new measures?" He replied, "When the chairman was about to leave Beijing yesterday, the reporters in Beijing also asked this question. However, because the matter is important, I was unable to give a definite answer. But today's situation in North China, although it cannot be said to be very optimistic, is absolutely not pessimistic. Now the people of North China are flocking south. The chairman has been ordered in times of crisis and resolutely took office and came north. There will definitely be a way. The chairman had a long conversation with President Wang yesterday when he was about to leave Beijing. The content is not convenient to disclose yet." "What is the chairman's mission when he sees Chairman Han in Jinan?" He replied, "Shandong is a part of North China, and Chairman Han is also a member of the North China Political Committee. The affairs of North China are all related to Shandong, so the chairman has something to discuss with Chairman Han. Furthermore, Chairman Han is the highest-ranking official in a province. When passing through this place, he must of course get off the train to show respect. There is also the fact that Chairman Huang and Chairman Han of this province have a teacher-student relationship, and Mr. He (Qigong) and Chairman Han are also former comrades-in-arms. After many years of separation, they also want to meet and reminisce." (3) "What is the policy direction after the establishment of the Political Committee?" He replied, "The North China Political Committee is an affiliated agency of the Executive Yuan and will of course follow the policy direction of the Executive Yuan. The jurisdiction of the Political Committee is Shandong, Hebei, Chahar, and Suiyuan provinces, and Beijing City."

Going North After a Banquet 96

Chairman Han Fuju hosted a banquet for Huang and He Qigong at the provincial government, and invited Li Shuchun, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Wang Xiangrong, Director of the Department of Finance, Zhang Honglie, Director of the Department of Construction, He Siyuan, Director of the Department of Education, Wang Fangting, Director of the Department of Industry, Zhang Weicun, a member of the provincial government, and Zhang Shaotang, Secretary-General of the provincial government, to accompany them. They talked and laughed happily during the banquet. After the meal at 9 PM, Huang and He went to the station. Han Fuju, Wang Fangting, and Chai Dongsheng, etc., all went to the station to see them off. The Jinpu Railway Bureau had prepared a special train for Huang in Jinan in advance. Huang boarded the train and bid farewell to the farewell party one by one. At 9:40 PM, the train left Jinan for Beiping. Wang Kemin, a member of the North China Political Committee, also passed through Jinan yesterday on his way to Beiping. (May 17)

Wuxi 97

The Young Daughter Died and the Coffin Was Opened for Examination

In the 541st Tu of the 5th District of the county, in the Northwest Tang area, the death of A Rong, daughter of Wang Erquan, a villager, was unclear. There were various rumors outside, saying that she was injured in a rape attempt, or that she was injured by a fall due to fright. Zhou Erkai, the chief prosecutor of the county court, out of caution for human life, brought along the examining officer and others to the village to open the coffin for examination yesterday (the 18th). The examination revealed that the girl had a kick injury on her back, a bump injury on her forehead and left knee, and a punch injury on her right rib. It was indeed an injury sustained before death, which caused her illness and death the next day. After the examination, Wang Erquan was instructed to re-coffin and bury her and await further investigation.

The Chief of the Second Branch Bureau is Removed from Office and Investigated 98

Yan Shenyu, the magistrate of this county, has been in office for more than a month and is making every effort to rectify officialdom. The other day, Magistrate Yan was informed by Wu Dexin, the chief of the County Public Security Bureau, that Zhu Niansheng, the chief of the Second Branch Bureau of Public Security, had committed many misdeeds. He concealed and did not report cases of violations of police regulations and embezzled fines. He requested that he be dealt with according to the law. After receiving the report, Yan immediately ordered Jin Shiqi, the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau, to summon Zhu Niansheng to the county. Magistrate Yan personally interrogated him. Zhu's confession was vague, only admitting that he had failed to supervise. Magistrate Yan then additionally summoned Wu Xiqing and Sun Shizhao, two employees of the branch bureau, to the county for questioning. As a result, Magistrate Yan personally ordered Zhu Niansheng to be removed from office and investigated, and handed him over to Inspector Jin for custody. Wu Xiqing and Sun Shizhao were detained. Yesterday (the 18th), he prepared a document and transferred Zhu and the other three to the county court for interrogation.

Changzhou 99

Zhu Xia Township Robbery and Assault

Shi Qingbao, the deputy chief of Zhu Xia Township in the 14th district of Wu County, and his son were both out doing business. Only his old wife and two daughters-in-law were at home, and their circumstances were well-off. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 16th, more than 20 bandits suddenly came, climbed over the wall and broke into the inner room. They immediately tied up Shi's two daughters-in-law with ropes, and then tortured Shi's wife, burning her lower body with fire. They searched and robbed for about three hours. The bandits guarding the wind also fired guns to intimidate. They left at dawn. On the morning of the 17th, the owner reported to the township district office, which has been transferred to the county to order the arrest of the stolen goods.

The Provincial Defense Council Sends Personnel to Assess 100

Cheng Jihou, a member sent by the Provincial Defense Committee, came to Changzhou to assess the defense corps in various places. County Magistrate Cai Pei, together with Committee Member Cheng and Liu Yuanchang, the director of the corps affairs of the County Defense Committee, and others, took a gasoline boat to Xiaxi in the third district to assess at about 6 AM on the 17th. He returned to Changzhou that night. He still had to go to various districts to assess in the coming days before returning to the province to report back.

Jiaxing 101

Silk Cocoon Market Loan Group Established

The silkworm farming in the four rural areas of Jiaxing has passed its third molt, and the new cocoons will be on the market soon. Various silk merchants are concentrating large sums of money to prepare to open factories to buy. The silver and money industry in Hedi also specially organized a loan group for the silk cocoon season of the silver and money industry in order to help the silk cocoon market. The fixed amount is 500,000 yuan. Each silk merchant who has 40,000 yuan can find a guarantor to borrow 60,000 yuan from the loan group. The term is three months, and the interest is calculated at one cent and one li. Everything is handled by the borrower. The Farmers Bank can only lend to rural cooperatives because it is restricted by provincial and ministerial departments, so it did not join the loan group.

Surveying the Airport on the Ping-Hu Line

The Ministry of Communications decided that airplanes on the Pinghu line should return to Shanghai from Haizhou. When they flew over the Nantong River, they encountered fog. If they flew over, there might be an accident. It would be a long journey to return to Haizhou. Therefore, it was decided to set up an airport in Nantong and build a radio station. On the 17th, the ministry sent a technical assistant, Yu Shipai, to survey the airport with County Magistrate Ye. It was decided to take over the 400-mu grassland in the Tangzha area.
