Gaoyou 103

Bandits Urge Ransom and Set Fire to Meat Tickets

Hongtao, the son of Yang Guozeng, a farmer in Jiangjiaxia, the ninth district of the county, was kidnapped by bandits last month. There has been no news of him so far. In the evening of the day before yesterday (14th), more than 20 bandits came to Yang's house again, twisted Guozeng and told him to first raise 1,000 yuan and send it to Sanlang Temple to get his son back. The remaining 1,000 yuan would be taken by someone after the autumn harvest. If he failed to do so, they would burn down the entire village, killing everyone, including chickens and dogs. When the bandits were about to leave, they set fire to the grass stacks in each house, fired their guns and fled.

Bengbu 104

Salt Industry Disputes Rise Again

The salt industry association here believes that the commission earned by more than 1,000 salt merchants in more than 50 salt firms in the whole city is too low, making it difficult to maintain a livelihood. It was agreed that an additional eight cents would be added to the original commission of one jiao and two fen per dan of salt. Lu Jianzhai and 20 other merchants believed that the salt firms had increased the commission without authorization, increasing the burden on the people. They strongly opposed it and filed lawsuits with governments at all levels and the 　 official office, requesting to stop the levy in order to relieve the people's suffering. After the Anhui provincial government explicitly banned it, the firms only collected five cents. Lu and others believed that the tax inspection association had illegally collected more than 10,000 yuan in the past month or so and should hand it over in full for local public welfare. The salt industry associations did not believe that they had illegally collected so much and signed and handed over 2,000 yuan. Lu and others still went ahead and requested that they be recovered. It was required that all be handed over. Now a certain 　　 is mediating and negotiating. It is heard that the salt industry is complaining to governments at all levels and the salt affairs competent official office that the commission earned by themselves is too little and is actually restricted by the North Salt Public Business Office, pleading for the abolition of the office, and will not stop until the goal is achieved. It seems that there will be a major dispute in the salt case here again.

Page 9

Local News

International Radio Station and Mackay Company Announce 105

An Additional Set of Lines Between China and the United States Scheduled to Open Today

National News Agency reports that the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications and the Mackay Radio Telegraph Company have been planning to communicate with each other for some time. It is now learned that the two parties have agreed to start communicating today. From now on, a new set of lines will be added to the world's communication network, bringing China and the rest of the world closer and making news more accessible. At a time when countries around the world are paying attention to events in the Far East, it is particularly thought-provoking that the new lines are starting to communicate. The service contract signed between the Ministry of Communications and the Mackay Company allows the Ministry's existing international radio stations to communicate with the company's San Francisco radio stations. The company is part of the International Telephone and Telegraph Company, which has agencies for operating and managing wired telegraphs and telephones in various regions of the world. The most famous of these are Mackay Radio Telegraph Company, which specializes in transatlantic business between Europe and the United States, Commercial Cable Company, which specializes in all-American Telegraph Company between North America, South America, and the West Indies, and Postal Telegraph Company.

The history of the Mackay Company can be traced back to 1910, when wireless telegraph was created to compete with landline business. The operator was the American Federal Radio Telegraph Company, which established radio stations in major cities in the United States. Later, due to restrictions by the US government, it was only allowed to conduct commercial communications along the Pacific coast. The company's famous directional radio stations were established at this time. In 1917, the US government temporarily nationalized the company's stations because it joined the European War. In order to maintain its business, the company had to transmit its communications by wire, but because the efficiency of wire was far less than that of wireless, the company still engaged in the construction of wireless radio stations after the end of the European War in 1920. Since then, the business has developed day by day and has attracted the attention of the Postal Telegraph Company. In October of the same year, Mackay, the manager of the Postal Telegraph Company, devised a way to purchase the company's wireless part, and the Mackay Radio Telegraph Company was established at this time. Since then, Mackay Company began to build its international radio station in San Francisco to communicate with Honolulu and the Philippines, and the radio stations surpassing the Pacific Ocean were also completed at this time. In 1929, Mackay Company merged with the International Telephone and Telegraph Company again. Since returning to international company management, Mackay Company's business has become more and more prosperous. In the beginning, it could only conduct directional communications along the Pacific coast, but now it has trans-Atlantic circuits directly to Europe between Europe and the United States, and circuits to Cuba, Peru, Argentina, Corombu, and the West Indies in South America. On the Pacific side, there are radio stations in San Francisco, Honolulu, and the Philippines. Now the Ministry of Communications and the company have started to communicate with each other, and a new circuit has been opened in the Pacific Ocean. Telegrams sent from Shanghai to the eastern United States can be transmitted to New York via San Francisco, and telegrams sent to various regions in South America can also be forwarded via New York. If communications between China and the United States develop in the future, it will be easy to open a direct circuit from Shanghai to New York. Although Mackay Company and Postal Telegraph Company are separate organizations, they are jointly operated on the transmission and reception of communications. Postal Telegraph Company has as many as 70,000 communication agencies in the United States. The two companies are both under the management of the International Telephone and Telegraph Company, so there is no need to borrow other people's routes for transmission and reception, and the transmission is naturally faster.

From China's perspective, communicating with Mackay Company not only increases the country's income, but also opens up a new set of lines, which can increase international traffic and prevent the monopoly of other companies. The benefits are indeed many.

Rumors of Two Northern Compromise Conditions 106

The Japanese Side Expresses Hope for Realization

New Voice Agency reports that yesterday's British newspaper North China Daily News reported that the Sino-Japanese military issue in the north has been resolved. Under two conditions, namely (1) both sides understand that if the Chinese army stays south of the Luan River, the Japanese army will withdraw to outside the Great Wall; (2) do not encourage or supply the Volunteer Army to disrupt "Manchukuo." The spokesperson of the Japanese Embassy denied this when talking to a reporter from the New Voice Agency who visited yesterday, but believed that these conditions could be accepted by the Japanese military. However, this compromise may not be so rapid. This is because the attitudes of both China and Japan are now quite tough, and it is not easy to make their opinions gradually converge. But it is believed that both sides may compromise under these conditions. However, on the other hand, Huang Fu, the newly appointed chairman of the North China Political Reorganization Committee, has denied the compromise business, and Huang has also declared that he will never sign any agreement. Also, some Japanese soldiers have advocated an extremely tough attitude. Although Huang is a person who is insightful about the situation in Japan and has a fairly good relationship with Japan, under these circumstances, the saying of compromise seems to be slim. However, in terms of realistic situations, there is a slight turning point in the north. Since Huang arrived in Ping, Huang has said that he will seek a temporary peace solution under mutual understanding. It can be imagined that the realization of a disguised compromise is only a matter of time.

Chen Ying Shi Memorial Meeting 107

Held separately by the City Party Headquarters and the Lake Society

May 18th is the anniversary of the martyrdom of Mr. Chen Ying Shi, a martyr of the Nationalist Party. The City Party Headquarters of this city convened people from all walks of life at 9:00 am to hold the 17th Anniversary Memorial Meeting for the Martyrdom of Mr. Chen Ying Shi. Members of the Lake Society also held a public memorial ceremony at the Ying Shi Memorial Hall on Guizhou Road. The details of the memorial meeting and the public memorial ceremony are recorded separately below:

Memorial at the Party Headquarters 108

Order of the Meeting: (1) Opening; (2) Singing the Party Song; (3) Paying the highest respect to the Party and National Flags and the portrait of the Premier; (4) The Chairman respectfully reading the Premier's Will; (5) Silent tribute for three minutes in memory of the Martyr Chen Ying Shi; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Speeches; (8) Shouting slogans; (9) Conclusion.

Attendees: Zheng Letian of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Xie Baochen of the Postal Administration, Zhang Mengling of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Yu Zhenhui of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Pan Rongting of the South Shanghai District Farmers' Association, Shao Xubai of the General Labour Union, Liu Yongkang of the Pharmaceutical Industry Association, Lu Muqin of the Pharmaceutical Trade Association, Zhu Chengdong of the First District Rubber Industry Union, Jiang Xiangcai of the Qin Industry Union, Wei Dongshan of the Pig Industry Union, Fan Guoren of the First Special District Citizens' Federation, Liu Pingji of the Women's Suffrage Association, Hu Xiongting of Jiaotong University, Jingye Middle School, Huadong Middle School, Junyi Middle School, Shihua, Longde, Bide, Feihong, and other primary schools, as well as representatives from various district party headquarters and branches, and all staff members of the City Party Headquarters, more than 300 people.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Pan Gongzhan reported, briefly stating that seventeen years ago, on this day, Mr. Chen Ying Shi, a martyr of our party, was ambushed by Yuan Shikai's henchmen at his residence on Sapo Sai Road in this city. Mr. Ying Shi's revolutionary spirit is known to all. Mr. Ying Shi participated in the revolution and sacrificed himself for the revolution. What we admire most about him is the spirit of obedience and hard work. What Mr. Ying Shi obeyed was the revolutionary doctrine and the orders of the revolutionary leader. What Mr. Ying Shi worked hard at was the revolutionary cause. Mr. Ying Shi went to Japan eight years before the founding of the Republic of China, joined the Tongmenghui, followed Sun Yat-sen, planned the revolution, and took on difficult tasks. During the uprisings in various places in 1911, Mr. Ying Shi personally participated in the secret planning. After the Wuhan Uprising, he gathered comrades in Shanghai and took the lead in responding, recovering Shanghai, serving as the military governor of Shanghai, assisting the allied forces of various provinces, laying the foundation for the southeast, and promoting unification. However, when we recall the difficulties Mr. Ying Shi encountered when he launched the revolution in Shanghai, it is impossible to express them in a few words. Mr. Ying Shi disregarded everything and sacrificed himself for the revolution with his spirit of hard work. In the end, Mr. Ying Shi's ability to cope recovered Shanghai. Since the founding of the Republic of China, Mr. Ying Shi has always followed Sun Yat-sen, taking the Premier's will as his will and striving for revolution. Mr. Ying Shi only knew obedience to the Premier. Today, when we commemorate Mr. Ying Shi, we should deeply recognize his spirit of obedience and hard work. When we look at the current disorganization of our party's organization and the abandonment of discipline, and the increasingly deteriorating situation, which has led to the country's increasingly declining fortunes, some people believe that the current crisis in China cannot be saved by our party alone and that we need to unite with other factions. This is due to the reduction of self-confidence. We can certainly see the difficulties encountered in the past revolutionary efforts in China, or even worse than today, but the revolutionary patriots of our party will eventually break through this difficult situation. Therefore, what we need today is to hope that all party comrades can follow Mr. Ying Shi's spirit of obedience and hard work, then our party can still restore the revolutionary atmosphere of the past and have a day of revival.

Meeting Slogans: (1) Mr. Chen Ying Shi is a believer in the Three Principles of the People; (2) Mr. Chen Ying Shi is a pioneer in resisting feudal remnants; (3) To commemorate Mr. Chen Ying Shi, we must work hard to suppress bandits and resist Japan; (4) The spirit of Mr. Chen Ying Shi is immortal; (5) Long live the Republic of China; (6) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party; (7) Long live the Three Principles of the People.

Chen Pagoda Opens: The Chen Ying Shi Memorial Pagoda in Ximen, after the municipal government allocated funds for its construction and completion, stands tall and magnificent. The pagoda gate is usually tightly closed, and citizens are not allowed to enter. Later, it was stipulated that it would be open for one day every year on Mr. Ying Shi's memorial day for public viewing. Yesterday, it was opened from 9:00 am, and many citizens climbed the pagoda. Last night, the retro-reflective lights installed on the poles around the pagoda were turned on to illuminate the top of the pagoda, so that citizens could admire it.

Public Memorial Ceremony at the Lake Society 109

Order of the Public Memorial Ceremony: (1) Opening; (2) Playing mourning music; (3) Singing the Party Song; (4) Paying the highest respect to the Party and National Flags and the portrait of the Premier; (5) The Chairman respectfully reading the Premier's Will; (6) Silent tribute for three minutes; (7) Public memorial ceremony: (A) Offering flowers, (B) Bowing three times, (C) Reading the memorial text, (D) Singing the elegy; (8) Reporting on the deeds of the martyr and the circumstances of his death; (9) Speeches; (10) Family expresses gratitude; (11) Playing mourning music; (12) Conclusion.

Mourning Situation: The meeting opened at 10:00 am. Chairman Tang Jicang conducted the ceremony as required. The chief celebrant, Wang Yiting, offered flowers, Shen Tianxin read the memorial text, and the students of Ying Shi Primary School sang the elegy. Then, the chairman reported on the deeds of the martyr and the circumstances of his death. Afterwards, Pan Gongzhan, the representative of the City Party Headquarters, delivered a speech. Finally, the Chen family expressed their gratitude and the meeting concluded.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Tang Jicang reported, briefly stating that everyone present was probably familiar with Mr. Chen Gong Ying Shi's deeds and the circumstances of his death and there was no need to repeat them. At today's public memorial ceremony, it was felt that the participants were all young people. Young people are the pillars of the country and will surely continue the unfinished ambitions of the martyrs and jointly plan the national affairs. When Mr. Chen was alive, he was brave in seeing things and doing things, and he never gave up despite setbacks, which led to his tragic death. However, although Mr. Chen is dead, his great spirit still exists and is a model for our young people, and so on.

Chairman's Welcome Speech 114

We are extremely honored that Mr. Martin has honored us with his presence today and gathered with our colleagues. Mr. Martin is the famous chief writer of the Geneva Newspaper, the center of world opinion, and Geneva is also the location of the conference that presides over the fair trial of the Far East Sino-Japanese issue. The Far East issue has been discussed at the conference many times, and Mr. Martin has personally heard and witnessed it. Therefore, the opinions published in the newspaper can be fair and not be misled by the Japanese side's one-sided propaganda. Japanese imperialism is taking advantage of the world's troubles and using its new weapons such as airplanes to put pressure on us. Now it has even invaded Pingjin. It is undeniable that our country is weak and cannot resist it, but we dare to be confident that we will never succumb in the end and will eventually seek self-salvation through our own efforts. Therefore, we do not dare to excessively hope that the League of Nations will provide any assistance. We only hope that the League of Nations will abide by its charter and handle the matter thoroughly and fairly. At the same time, we also hope that Mr. Martin can use his authority to guide world opinion, judge the right and wrong of the Sino-Japanese issue, and fully publicize all the atrocities of the Japanese warlords, so that all countries in the world can understand the truth. The light of world peace depends on this, which is what we all hope for. Now, please join me in a toast to Mr. Martin's health and ask him to enlighten us.

Mr. Martin's Reply 115

Fellow comrades, I am deeply grateful for the grand banquet hosted by the Shanghai Newspaper Association today. I personally feel that this gathering can be called a meal for colleagues, which has a profound meaning. As a European journalist, I have many purposes for coming to China this time, but the most important one is to visit your country and get close to your people to exchange ideas. When I was in Geneva, I often felt that hearing about the situation in your country was not as good as seeing it with my own eyes. This time, I came to China in person and was very happy and honored to have a meal with my colleagues in the Chinese press.

Mr. Martin's Speech 116

In addition to sightseeing, I intend to use a method to make Article 16 of the Covenant of the League of Nations effective. I have been in Geneva for eighteen months. Although the region is small, it has a great impact on the world, because important people from all over the world often gather here to discuss major issues in order to solve everything. The Geneva Daily, which I run in Geneva, does not have a large circulation due to the small area and population, but most important people like to read the newspaper and often use the newspaper's remarks as a source of conversation. This is because the newspaper's remarks have always been fair. In Geneva, I am also striving for fairness and justice. If world justice can be maintained, then the Sino-Japanese dispute will be easily resolved fairly. I have always had extremely friendly feelings towards your country, but I am not very clear about the situation in your country. Initially, the representatives sent by your country to Geneva were very few, and no major issues occurred. When the September 18th Incident occurred, I wanted to investigate the truth of the case, so I went to the Japanese consulate to visit Saito and asked him to explain everything, but what he said was not something I dared to believe. Therefore, I still maintained my consistent position and spoke out for justice, which caused displeasure from the Japanese side. Because my view on the September 18th Incident has expanded the issue and made it a world peace issue, not just a dispute between China and Japan. This not only exposed Japan's weakness, but I firmly believe that justice will prevail one day. As for what the chairman said that China will never succumb and is determined to resist to the end, I feel very happy to hear it. I dare to predict that your country, with this determination, will be the creator of justice prevailing over power in the near future.

The Executive Yuan Orders All Provinces and Municipal Governments

To Prepare for the Restoration of Rural Organizations 122

The Shanghai Municipal Government Has Ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to Handle It

Appendix: Nine Articles of the Rural Revival Regulations

The Municipal Government of this city previously received Executive Yuan Order No. 2031, which stated that for the purpose of restoring the countryside, a Rural Revival Committee would be established to formulate regulations and order the governments of all provinces and municipalities to promulgate and implement them immediately. It is also learned that the Municipal Government ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to prepare for handling it the day before yesterday. The Executive Yuan's order and the promulgated Rural Revival Committee Regulations are recorded below:

Order 123

For order to be followed, I have investigated the 96th meeting of this Yuan. The President proposed that the national countryside is in decline and that a committee should be organized to plan relief measures. Please make a public decision on this case. It was resolved to be handed over to the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Industry, together with the Secretariat and Political Affairs Office of this Yuan, to jointly discuss the organization method and submit it for verification on record. Now, according to the draft regulations of the Rural Committee proposed by the departments and offices, please review and verify them. After being submitted to the 97th meeting of this Yuan, it was resolved to be amended and passed, and Peng Xuepei was appointed as the director of the Secretariat of the Rural Revival Committee. In addition to submitting it to the National Government for record and issuing separate letters of order, a copy of the regulations is hereby issued for your information. This order includes a copy of the Rural Revival Committee Regulations.

Regulations 124

(Article 1) The Executive Yuan of the National Government shall establish a Rural Revival Committee for the purpose of planning methods for reviving the countryside, raising funds for revival, and subsidizing the progress of revival projects. (Article 2) The Committee shall be located in Nanjing. (Article 3) The members of the Committee shall be appointed by the President of the Executive Yuan. The President and Vice President of the Executive Yuan and the ministers of the relevant ministries (Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Industry, Ministry of Communications, Ministry of Railways) shall be ex officio members. The President of the Yuan shall also serve as the Chairman of the Committee. When the meeting is held, the relevant ministries may send one deputy minister to attend. The ministers of other ministries, the chairmen of various committees, the chairmen of provincial governments, the mayors of directly administered cities, the Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, and the Director of the Political Affairs Office may attend and participate at any time. (Article 4) The Committee may divide into groups such as rural finance, rural technology, grain regulation, and water conservancy to plan separately, and may also set up various specialized committees. Specialized committee members shall be appointed by the Chairman of the Committee. (Article 5) Committee members and specialized committee members shall all be unpaid positions, but the Chairman of the Committee may provide travel expenses if deemed necessary. (Article 6) The Committee shall set up a Secretariat. The staff shall be transferred from the staff of various agencies by the Chairman of the Committee without additional salary. Travel expenses may be provided when necessary (The Secretariat shall have one director who shall handle all affairs of the Committee under the command of the Chairman). (Article 7) The Committee may send personnel to inspect and assist in the implementation of various plans. (Article 8) All stationery, postal, and telegraphic expenses required by the Committee shall be provided by the Executive Yuan. In addition, investigation fees, hospitality fees, book fees, printing fees, and travel expenses shall be reimbursed after actual reporting after the Executive Yuan has determined the scope. (Article 9) These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Executive Yuan.

Principal and Interest Totaling More Than 500,000 National Currency

When the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway was nationalized, the former Beijing Ministry of Communications borrowed funds from the Sino-British Bank to repay commercial shares. County Agricultural Product Exhibition 126

The Second Preparatory Meeting Was Held Yesterday

Please Invite Cao Zhenfei as the President

The Opening Ceremony is Scheduled for June 10th

Since the Shanghai County Second Agricultural Product Exhibition was entrusted by the County Government to Zhang Yi as the preparation director to carry out the preparatory work, it has been actively carried out and has solicited many items. The meeting was originally scheduled to be held at the same time as the relocation ceremony, but due to various reasons, the relocation ceremony was difficult to hold for a while. Director Zhang specifically convened district chiefs, directors of social education institutions, directors of agricultural affairs institutions, agricultural experts, and administrative authorities at the county government auditorium yesterday to hold the second preparatory meeting. The attendees were Peng Liren, Zhang Jingye, Jin Zuobin, Zhang Weibin, Li Jianye, Gong Xianglin, Zhu Hange, Ding Baizheng, Zhu Ruoxi, Shen Jing, Peng Yinqiao, Wu Shifang, Zheng Lizhai, Yang Huiming, Shi Yangyong, Zheng Shaoyuan, Cao Zhenfei (on behalf of Li Tongrui), and Zhang Yi. The meeting was presided over by Zhang Yi and recorded by Zheng Shaoyuan. After the ceremony, the following matters were discussed: (1) Determination of the exhibition location, resolved to be the County Government Auditorium. (2) Stipulation of the exhibition dates, resolved to be June 10th, 11th, and 12th for three days. (3) Adding recreational activities related to agricultural improvement during the exhibition period to promote publicity, resolved to organize a recreational department to plan and carry out. (4) Various social education institutions and agricultural affairs institutions should pay attention to the production of comparable and systematic products for demonstration purposes, resolved that each institution should have at least one product (choose one from wheat, wheat, and rapeseed), and then notify them to pay attention. (5) To appoint various institutions to be responsible for the affairs of each department, resolved to be the arrangement department: County Government Liangxing Min Education Hall, Tangwan Min Education Hall; Guidance Department: Agricultural Improvement Station, Agricultural Extension Area; Custody Department: County Education Bureau; Reception Department: each institution should recommend one person; Affairs Department: County Education Bureau, Property Office; Recreational Department: Zhuanqiao Agricultural Education Hall; Editorial Department: County Party Department, County Government, County Education Bureau, Agricultural Improvement Station, Qiangshu Horticulture School. (6) To hire referees, resolved to be hired by the president. (7) To hire the president of the association, resolved to hire the county magistrate as the president. (8) Should the meals of the staff be provided, resolved that the meals of the staff of each department of the association should be provided. (9) How should the outstanding farmers participating in the exhibition be rewarded, resolved to be determined after the refereeing is over. (10) Determining the date of refereeing, resolved to be June 11th. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Dependents of the Generals of Li Du's Troops Arrived in Shanghai from Beiping 127

They Will Arrive Today

The 30 family members of the generals of Li Du's troops, the commander-in-chief of the Jilin Self-Defense Army, retreated into Russia with General Li Du. They then returned to China via Vladivostok and temporarily resided in Beiping. Because Pingjin was in danger, no one took care of them, and there were problems with food and lodging. They had no choice but to leave Beiping for Shanghai the night before last, led by Madam Xie Yiqing, the wife of Li Du. It is expected that they will arrive in Shanghai this evening. Liu Piguang, Li Du's representative in Shanghai, contacted various groups yesterday to discuss the accommodation and food issues for the family members of Li's troops after they arrived in Shanghai. As for General Li Du's arrival in Shanghai in early June, the troops of Li's troops who arrived in Xinjiang decided to stay in Xinjiang Province and wait for the government to reorganize them before guarding the border. There are still 30,000 troops of Li's troops remaining in Jilin, and they are still continuing their activities.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce notified all industries yesterday

Custody of the Qinghe Hotel Customer's Suicide by Poison 130

Around 12 o'clock the night before last, a traveler arrived at the Qinghe Hotel, number 181, Qinghefang Alley, Wuma Road, Zhejiang Road. He claimed to be a local named Miao Fengyi, 21 years old, a businessman. It is unknown why, but he had thoughts of suicide and ingested raw opium. The next morning around 12 o'clock, the tea attendant knocked on the door, but there was no response, which was quite strange. So, he found a way to pry the door open and saw Miao lying stiff on the bed, having been dead for a long time. He immediately notified the accounting office and reported to the police station, who ordered detectives to the scene to carry the body to Renji Hospital and then to the morgue for examination.

Scrap Iron Smelting Injures Laborers 131

The Yiyuan Copper and Tin Shop, number 51, Tongqing Street, Xiaobeimen, Min'guo Road, specializes in collecting all kinds of scrap goods, copper, and tin raw materials. At 7:30 last night, the shop was smelting scrap iron when, not long after it was put into the pot, the scrap iron unexpectedly contained explosives. With a loud bang, two laborers were injured on the spot: Zhang Minli, 23 years old, from Jiangbei, was injured all over his body; Chen Defa, 19 years old, a local, was injured in his hands, head, and other parts. They were later taken to Renji Hospital by carriage for treatment.

Unemployed and Bored, Arson Attempt for Compensation 132

Zhou Xunfu, a Ningbo native who used to run a foreign goods business and lived at number 13, Sanyi Lane, Bail'er Road, in the French Concession, had insured his property for 1,000 taels with the Hua'an Insurance Company last year. Recently, due to unemployment and boredom, he plotted to obtain insurance compensation. On the morning of the 28th of last month, at 2 a.m., while his housemate was asleep, he used a lighter and a handkerchief to set a fire. Then, he and his wife fled. The fire was extinguished by the fire brigade. Chief Detective Tao Desheng and Detective Bao Jinrong of the French Concession police investigated and arrested Zhou, transferring him to the Second Special Court for public prosecution. The details of the interrogation were recorded in previous reports. The case was subsequently investigated by Judge Wang Gangxu, head of the criminal court, who personally inspected the scene. The trial has concluded, and yesterday, Judge Wang sentenced Zhou Xunfu to three years and six months of imprisonment for the crime of arson and destruction of a currently used residence. The defendant, upon hearing the verdict, declared in court that he was not satisfied and requested an appeal. The court granted the request and ordered him to be remanded to the detention center pending further instructions.

Chinese Workers Demand Back Wages from Japanese 133

Shun Pao Telegraph Agency Local News: The Japanese military barracks on Jiangwan Road were destroyed by our army's artillery fire during the January 28th Incident. The Japanese side specially rebuilt a large-scale barracks on the original site last winter. For several months, it has not been completed. The construction project was contracted by the Ogura Construction Company of Japan, which hired more than 40 Japanese workers to be responsible for wood piles, steel bars, and other projects, and 800 laborers, specializing in transporting materials and other odd jobs. More than 100 workers were recruited from Qingdao to be responsible for the construction of the interior layout project. Later, due to the busy work, the original workers were not enough, so they entrusted the Japanese Matsumoto Ueo,

Who in turn entrusted Chinese Qian Jinbao and others to hire more than 100 Chinese workers. The wages for each person per day were divided into several types: one yuan, five jiao, and three jiao, etc. After starting work, the workers initially were able to receive wages according to the original agreement, but soon Matsumoto was in arrears, paying only half of the wages. To date, the amount owed has been very large. Last month, Matsumoto received 3,600 yuan in wages from Ogura, but did not pay a penny to the Chinese workers. The workers felt that Matsumoto had embezzled their hard-earned wages for his own benefit, and they expressed their unwillingness to continue working. Matsumoto was very embarrassed, so he negotiated with the workers, willing to provide them with rice every day in lieu of wages, and promised

To raise funds and pay back wages. The workers then agreed to resume work. Recently, Ogura, believing that Matsumoto's contracting of the construction project was progressing slowly, intended to terminate the contract with Matsumoto and contract it out to someone else. At the same time, they ordered more than 100 Chinese workers to stop working. The workers, since the work was stopped, wanted to settle the arrears with Matsumoto. After several contacts, Matsumoto had not given a definite answer. The workers, unwilling to let Matsumoto

Embezzle their hard-earned wages, specially gathered more than 100 workers at around 10 a.m. yesterday at Matsumoto Ueo's residence at number 29, Qiuzhi Lane, North Sichuan Road, to negotiate. They elected Wan Chengsheng and more than 10 others as representatives to meet with Matsumoto and demand wages, while the others sat on the ground in the lane and waited. The Fifth District Third Police Station, fearing that the crowd would cause trouble, sent translator Chen, along with the police chief and others, to the scene to suppress the situation,

To mediate. At the same time, the Fifth District Police Station also sent translator Li with police to assist in questioning Matsumoto. Negotiations continued until noon, when Matsumoto finally agreed to find a way to raise funds and pay the arrears. However, the workers insisted on a settlement at that time. After repeated persuasion and guidance by the two translators, Chen and Li, Matsumoto finally agreed to first distribute several bags of rice to the workers and then find a way to raise the remaining amount. At this point, the workers agreed to postpone the settlement temporarily.

Refugees Passing Through Cause Disturbances 134

The Huacun Temple in Nanshou, Hongqiao Town, West Shanghai, suddenly saw a total of 220 male and female refugees from Hunan Province arrive the day before yesterday. They are temporarily living in the temple and have been there for five days. However, there are too few houses and too many people, resulting in overcrowding. In the past two days, the refugees have been forming groups, going to nearby villages, asking for donations from house to house, and arbitrarily catching chickens and ducks, and stealing broad beans from the fields. The villagers, unable to bear the disturbance, rushed to report to the Hongqiao Town Police Station of the First Branch of the Sixth District, requesting that the police be dispatched to drive them away. Upon receiving the report, Police Chief Pan Xuezeng immediately led all armed police to the scene to suppress the situation and ordered the entire team to leave the country within two hours, prohibiting them from staying to avoid disturbances.

Fire Burns Candy Workshop 135

Also Affects Sino-French Laundry

At 11:50 last night, a fire broke out in the Wanlixiang Candy Workshop at number 97, Lafayette Road, in the French Concession, due to a cigarette butt. The flames immediately shot through the roof, and the fire was unstoppable, immediately burning down the entire floor. It also affected the upstairs of the Sino-French Laundry at number 95 next door. The fire brigade rushed to the scene and made every effort to put out the fire, which was extinguished only at 0:30 this morning.

Postal Workers' Union Advocates for Using National Products 137

Organizing a Committee to Promote the Use of National Products

Starting with Members' Clothing

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, in view of the profound national crisis and the urgency of foreign troubles, believes that promoting national products is an essential strategy for saving the country. Therefore, the executive committee of the union resolved to organize a committee to promote the use of national products, starting with the adoption of national products for members' clothing, and gradually promoting other daily necessities. Fan Caicong and six others were appointed as committee members to actively carry out the plan. The union is currently investigating and contacting various textile manufacturers to inquire about the quality and price of national products in order to make purchases. During the contact period, the union will be happy to adopt and introduce high-quality products from national product manufacturers who introduce them to the union.

Savings & Remittance Bureau

Focus of the Merger Issue 138

Ministry Side: Formulate separate regulations for appointment of savings & remittance employees

Labor Side: Must pass exams to be included in the postal service's regular ranks

The issue of merging the Savings & Remittance Bureau has been discussed in several meetings by the Postal Economic System Research Committee. Starting from May 10th, three consecutive meetings were held to discuss it in detail, and there are generally no more problems. The focus of the dispute is how to deal with the current employees of the Savings & Remittance Bureau at all levels. According to the responsible committee members of the labor and employee unions, the Ministry's representative believes that separate methods of appointment should be formulated in accordance with the inherent rules and regulations of the post office. According to the views of the employees, since the Savings & Remittance Bureau is merged into the General Post Office, its organization should be unified. If the Ministry insists on formulating separate regulations, it is tantamount to making the Savings & Remittance Bureau independent. Moreover, some of the current employees of the bureau have been transferred from the post office. If separate regulations are formulated in the future, which regulations will govern the various benefits, etc., of the post office personnel serving in the bureau? The current employees of the Savings & Remittance Bureau at all levels lack a clear standard for staying or leaving, and their career prospects are inevitably affected. Yesterday afternoon, the labor and employee unions held an emergency joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees. Regarding this issue, they instructed the representatives attending the Postal Research Committee meeting today to insist on: (1) passing a screening examination; (2) being included in the postal service ranks; (3) receiving the same treatment as postal personnel. If this issue cannot be resolved, the representatives may announce their withdrawal at any time.

·Guangdong Native Association's Reorganization Committee

Telegram Urges Chen Jitang and Others to Take Office 139

The Reorganization Committee of the Guangdong Native Association in Shanghai yesterday sent telegrams to Chen Jitang, Bai Chongxi, Cai Tingkai, and others, which read: "To Commander-in-Chief Chen Bonan of Guangzhou, Deputy Commander-in-Chief Bai Jiansheng of Nanning, and Commander-in-Chief Cai Tingkai of Fuzhou, with respect: The violent Japanese are invading, and the foreign troubles are becoming increasingly urgent. The communist bandits are rampant, and the internal troubles have not ended. To pacify the interior and resist foreign aggression, the central government has the determination, but the local governments should share the responsibility. Otherwise, the soldiers will be exhausted internally, and the enemy will be emboldened externally. The fate of the country is unbearable to imagine. You are leading the troops and serving as the bulwark of the country. The central government has entrusted you with the important responsibility of suppressing the communists. Taking office and setting out is the deep expectation of the people. We urge you to take office as soon as possible and shoulder the great hardship of resisting Japan. Do not hesitate or decline again, delaying the troops for resisting Japan. Then, the country will be revitalized through adversity, which will not be far away. Protecting the country and eliminating tyranny, the merits will be equal. At this critical moment, please do not hesitate. We anxiously await your response. The Reorganization Committee of the Guangdong Native Association in Shanghai, respectfully."

Ministry of Finance Approves the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Import of Used Gunny Sacks Not Allowed Tax Exemption 141

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received a request from the Yarn and Gunny Sack Industry Association to forward to the Ministry of Finance a request that used gunny sacks be treated in the same way as other empty containers and that the customs be ordered to uniformly exempt them from import duties. The Ministry of Finance has now replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating: "We have received your report and learned that used gunny sacks should be taxed in accordance with the tariff regulations. The request in the report that used gunny sacks be exempt from import duties when shipped to Shanghai is difficult to approve. You are hereby notified of this approval."

Customs Revises Import Tax on Bird's Nest and Ginseng 142

The Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs and the Commissioner of Customs yesterday issued a joint proclamation stating: "It has been found that the tariff rates for items 278 and 328 of the import tariff have now been amended by order of the government as follows, and will be implemented from May 17, 1933. All merchants are hereby notified." The amended import tariff is as follows: Item 276, Bird's Nest: (A) Raw Bird's Nest (including picked clean bird's nest layers), tax rate of 40% ad valorem; (B) White Bird's Nest, tax rate of 40% ad valorem. Item 328, Picked Clean American Ginseng, Unpicked Clean American Ginseng (including ginseng whiskers, ginseng stems, and broken ginseng, excluding wild ginseng): (A) Superior (value per catty over 61.25 gold units), tax rate of 40% ad valorem; (B) Second Class (value per catty over 43.75 gold units but not exceeding 61.25 gold units), tax rate of 40% ad valorem; (C) Third Class (value per catty over 19.25 gold units but not exceeding 43.75 gold units), tax rate of 40% ad valorem; (D) Fourth Class (value per catty over 10.5 gold units but not exceeding 19.25 gold units), tax rate of 40% ad valorem; (E) Fifth Class (value per catty over 5.25 gold units but not exceeding 10.5 gold units), tax rate of 40% ad valorem; (F) Sixth Class (value per catty not exceeding 5.25 gold units), tax rate of 40% ad valorem.

Dr. Fu Youren's Lecture 143

Last Sunday, Dr. Fu Youren continued his lecture on "The Resurrection of China," Part II, "The China of the Past," stating that the fundamental causes of China's current predicament can be divided into three categories: (1) the ancient influence of climate and geography, which cultivated a habit of easily relating the body to matter and the spirit to difficulty; (2) the old principles of China, which originated in the north and later spread to the central and southern regions, relying on memory for their dissemination. The danger of memory is that it prevents the true use of the brain; the third cause is the combination of the first two, namely, the first two causes make the Chinese feel a decline in strength. After this decline in strength, any plan for life or work is not thorough. It is heard that the third part, "The China of the Future," will continue to be lectured next Sunday (20th). This is the center of the entire topic, discussing how China can find a way out of this difficult intersection. Mr. Fu uses the latest Western psychology to explain this way out in detail. The address is still No. 468, Daxi Road (opposite Yuan Yuan Ranch). The time is 4:30 p.m. on May 20th (Sunday).

Xu Shiying, Chairman of the National Government Relief Committee, believes that the overseas Chinese who have returned from Mexico are destitute and deserve assistance. Yesterday, he ordered the committee's Shanghai office to telegraph the Beijing headquarters, allocating 2,000 yuan for relief.

British American Tobacco Factory Workers Resume Work Yesterday Morning 145

Workers at the Third Factory Continue to Strike

After the British American Tobacco factory's three-factory joint strike due to wage cuts, the municipal party and government agencies mediated the dispute a few days ago and decided to temporarily work four days a week, which was agreed upon by both labor and management. Four reconciliation measures were agreed upon. Yesterday morning, the Cigarette Industry Union of the Fifth District notified the workers of the first and second factories to resume work and immediately prepared a document to report the resumption of work to the Municipal Party Department's Social Affairs Bureau. However, the workers at the Yangshupu British American Tobacco Third Factory were not satisfied with the decided measures, and the detained workers were still not released, so the strike is still continuing.

Office Ordered to be Abolished Yesterday 147

To be Handled Directly by the Jiangsu Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau

Aviation Highway Lottery News from Beijing 151

The Aviation Highway Lottery Office announced that the lottery is tentatively divided into eight regions nationwide: Jiangzhe Region (including Shanghai and Nanjing), Shandong Region (including Qingdao), Hebei Region (including Tianjin and Peiping), Anhui Region, Exiangyu Region (including Hankou), Jiangxi Region, Sichuan Region, and Mingyuegui Region (including Guangzhou, Hong Kong, and Macau). The remaining provinces in the southwest, such as Yunnan and Guizhou, and the provinces in the west, such as Gansu, Shaanxi, Xinjiang, and Tibet, are not included due to inconvenient transportation and lack of responsible sales agents. The addresses of the general managers and managers in each region have been determined: Jin Tingsun for the Jiangzhe Region, with the general manager's office in Shanghai; Gao Xizhang for the Exiangyu Region, with the general manager's office in Hankou; Lu Bingyu for the Hebei Region, with the general manager's office in Tianjin; Shu Zhenting for the Anhui Region, with the general manager's office in Wuhu; Chen Xizhi for the Jiangxi Region; and a certain Hong Kong overseas merchant for the Fujian and Guangdong Regions, with the general manager's office in Hong Kong and Macau; Juxingcheng Bank for the Sichuan Region, with the general manager's office in Chongqing. The candidate for general manager of the Shandong Region has not yet been selected.

Robbery on Glock Road 152

The home of Zhu Xinquan, who runs a pawnshop business at No. 136, Jinxing Lane, north of Pishao Nai Road, Glock Road, in the French Concession, was suddenly visited by four or five robbers at noon the day before yesterday. They entered through the back door under the pretext of asking for a letter, and threatened with pistols. They ransacked the boxes and chests, stealing cash and jewelry worth more than 2,000 yuan, and fled in a crowd. It was found that Zhu's home was also robbed once in February last year, and Zhu's neighbors on both sides were also robbed one after another last year, suffering huge losses. The reason why robberies often occur in that area is that there are no police patrols, which emboldens the robbers to dare to commit robberies in broad daylight. It is now heard that the victim has issued a list of losses and reported to the police station, requesting a strict investigation and arrest in order to crack down on the bandits and reassure the people.

Publishing World 156

▲Discounted Western Books at the Commercial Press: The annual Western book discount sale at the Commercial Press was suspended last year due to the national crisis and was unable to take place. Although most of the books in stock were destroyed along with the main factory of the press, the distribution department still has as many as fifty to sixty thousand volumes in stock. It is now reported that the press has put these books on sale at discounted prices, with most selling for only one or two tenths of the original price, and at most, no more than half price. The press has prepared a catalog for free distribution, with a comparison of original and discounted prices. For example, Smallwood's New Biology, originally priced at US$2.70, is now priced at National Currency $2.70. Hogan's Outline of Radio, originally priced at US$2.00, is now priced at National Currency $2.00. Muscis's Lectures on Industrial Psychology, originally priced at 6 shillings and 6 pence, is now priced at National Currency 65 cents. Letter Received 161

To the Editor,

Having read in today's edition of your newspaper a Reuters news item stating, "The Shanghai Post Office issued a notice yesterday that postal items to Qinhuangdao and Changli are suspended due to the war," please note that the Shanghai Post Office has not issued a notice to suspend the acceptance of postal items to Qinhuangdao and Changli. All postal items are still being accepted and dispatched as usual. Correspondingly, this is to inform you, and I hope you will check and make an appropriate correction to the news in your newspaper tomorrow.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Postal Administration

National Humiliation Week Lecture

Mr. Zhang Naiqi's Views on the Future of Sino-Japanese Relations 162

Lecture at the YMCA on May 12th

When we study any social problem, we cannot escape examining its cause-and-effect relationship. We can only speculate on its future results if we know its past causes. The same is true when studying the Sino-Japanese problem. Let me start with the Japanese side:

First, aren't we always talking about examining a country's national character? A country's national character is neither good nor bad; it is only the result of being dominated by the environment. The reason why the Japanese national character is tough is due to their territory! Only four islands! Honshu, Shikoku, Kyushu, and Hokkaido, with an area of only 380,000 square kilometers (more than 23,000 square miles). After the Meiji Restoration, the introduction of Western culture further strengthened their weapons of plunder abroad, and they began to use all their strength to attack the weak nations nearby.

From 1874 (the 13th year of Tongzhi), they invaded Taiwan, then destroyed Ryukyu and changed it to Okinawa Prefecture; in 1895 (the 21st year of Guangxu), in the Sino-Japanese War, our country failed, and Japan carried out the seizure of Taiwan and the Penghu Islands; after the Russo-Japanese War in 1904, Japan won again, occupied the Liaodong Peninsula, and established the Kwantung Leased Territory; soon after, it reduced Korea; and then the Twenty-One Demands; the Shanghai Incident; the Jinan Massacre; and the recent September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident are all a continuous and consistent history of aggression. They have set their sights on the route, advancing north and south, with no disorder in their steps.

The cause of the September 18th Incident was the world economic panic, which produced a recession; the recession phenomenon spread around the globe. The fatal wound of capitalism lies in overproduction; overproduction leads to lower prices, increased unemployment, and social unrest; this is a natural trend. Japan, of course, could not escape this example. There was a left-right ideological commotion in the country, social unrest, and the Japanese government launched an attack on Shenyang. Economically, they could occupy all or part of Manchuria as a resource; politically, they could shift the eyes of the people outward to alleviate their own contradictions. This result led the Japanese from Liaoning to Jilin to Heilongjiang to Jehol, and recently they have even attempted to seize Beiping and Tianjin!

But again, we have to say that we ourselves are not good. Before the September 18th Incident, the Japanese intentionally or unintentionally hinted, such as the change of the Governor-General of Korea and the Governor-General of the South Manchuria Railway, the Wanbaoshan Incident, and the massacre of Chinese in Korea, all had the appearance of "a storm is brewing." Why didn't our government feel it? All because they were concentrating on their "internal pacification" work!

Now let's talk about why we don't resist. 1. The source of our country's finances is mainly customs duties and tobacco taxes, and its foundation is built on the treaty ports. If war is declared, the treaty ports may be blockaded. And the source of finance will be cut off. Then, in order to survive, we can only surrender and be slaughtered.

2. The current era is the era of colonial anti-imperialist movements, and the power of the anti-imperialist movement is very great. In a certain sense, it is enough to change our country's foreign policy to a policy of non-resistance.

So where is our way out in the future?

Now our only way out is to "fight," and there is no other way to go. My reasons for advocating fighting are: (1) Declaring war on the enemy will surely cause the country to focus its attention outward and no longer kill each other; (2) Declaring war on Japan is in line with the times. We know that the present era is the era of colonial anti-imperialism, and our country is one of the members of this anti-imperialist camp, and therefore our country cannot escape its responsibility and should meet it head-on!

From the enemy's point of view, the current Japanese invasion is accelerating the destruction of the rural economy; the collapse of the social and economic organization is becoming more thorough, which means that the objective conditions for the Chinese revolution are becoming more mature and urgent, forcing China to be pushed onto the path of revolution. At this time, if anyone dares to go against the times and advocate compromise, they will surely become the target of the revolution. The revolutionary masses should be 85% workers and peasants; they are unwilling to live under parasites anymore, and the environment is driving them to embark on the road of anti-imperialist vanguard. They have indeed been exploited enough, and they will never see the light unless they come out and overthrow their oppressors themselves.

However, if our country's revolutionary movement is launched, it will not be welcomed by the international capitalist imperialists. What they hope for is "don't move," and let them slaughter us. Sucking the marrow after the blood is exhausted! If our country revolts, we will not be favored by them. Our country's construction and the implementation of socialism and nationalism are not good for them. Their purpose is to call on us to compromise with them in order to maintain peace and protect the market, but we want to prolong our own lives, and we can only stand with them in a position of irreconcilable opposition.

So, if we go to war with Japan, can we be sure of victory?

From a historical point of view, the present is the era of the final backlash of the dying throes of capitalist imperialism. But no matter how it struggles, the result will inevitably tend to collapse, which is certain. On this point, we are confident in resisting Japan.

We see that Japan's current invasion of us has two purposes: first, to sell its surplus goods and shift internal contradictions outward.

But has Japan achieved this first purpose? We see that last year Japan's foreign trade decreased by 35% compared to the previous year. In principle, the devaluation of the Japanese yen last year should have increased its trade exports, but now it is trending downward, which shows that its desire to sell surplus goods is futile; looking at the current situation in Japanese society, ideology is still extremely left-leaning; order has not been seen to be at peace, which shows that his desire to shift internal contradictions outward is also a fantasy. Second, Japan wants to use Manchuria as a resource to be self-sufficient and resist the encroachment of surplus goods from international capitalist imperialism. However, the current economic panic is an overall global economic recession, and its fatal wound lies in the contradictions of capitalism itself, overproduction. Japan wants to use Manchurian resources alone to solve its difficulties under the entire world economic panic. Is this really possible? Moreover, after Japan seized Manchuria, it only increased its internal contradictions and economic chaos. Therefore, my conclusion is: first, if our country launches a full national revolution, it will definitely give a major shock to international capitalism, at least imperialism, and arouse the common struggle of oppressed nations around the world, otherwise, if we compromise with Japan, we will only sit and wait for death. Second, the launch of our country's entire national revolution is imminent. If we continue to delay, we will inevitably be divided up like melons and beans. (Recorded by Ye Wenxiong)

Spring and Autumn

Cool Words 163

— Baihe

The northwest wind has disappeared for a long time, and the apricot blossom spring rain has also been sent away by the literati and elegant scholars. These days, the thermometer indicating the hot and cold weather has risen from over forty, over fifty, over sixty, to over seventy. Although the news of "heatstroke deaths of dock workers" and "rickshaw pullers suffering from heatstroke" has not yet been revealed in the newspapers, and the tongue in the dog's mouth has not yet been hung out, Dutch water has already been launched on the market, ice cream has been selling well, people who look at each other have opened their cheongsam jackets, and laborers have exposed their upper bodies. Everything is already showing that it is very hot.

In the cold weather, it is indeed effective in eliminating cold and relieving cold to persuade people to be "enthusiastic about ××" and "enthusiastic about ××," but when the weather is hot, it is a bit inappropriate to persuade people to be "enthusiastic about ××" and "enthusiastic about ××." So, "cool words" deserve to be lucky.

What is there to fear about national subjugation? The Jews have been without a country for more than a thousand years, and the Jews are so prominent. Didn't Poland also be subjugated? Look, isn't it very good now? As for India, even Shaw is advocating allowing it to be independent. The Koreans are even more amazing, making the Japanese busy and flustered with their revolution. We Chinese have lost the three northeastern provinces, plus Jehol. Old Zhang has a lot of capital and doesn't care. Even if the Japanese iron cavalry treads from Beiping and Tianjin to the Yellow River, crosses the Yangtze River, and goes straight to the Pearl River, and the whole of China is subjugated, will it really be "one Japanese person monitoring one Chinese person"? Even if China is subjugated, there will be no revolution, so it is certain that it will be subjugated, so there is no need to worry. There are many more slaves in the world, and it is not just us Chinese. Moreover, Japan will inevitably have a major earthquake sooner or later, Tokyo will sink to the bottom of the sea, and the people will all commit suicide. Even if it is not like this, the Northeast should be recovered by us by the end of this year. Taking a hundred steps back, if it is not recovered by the end of this year, Japan will inevitably have a revolution within ten years and automatically abandon the Northeast. In fact, these are all nonsense. How can China be subjugated? The Communists have exhausted their strength and will soon be united against foreign enemies and recover lost territory according to their consistent predetermined policy.

We ordinary people can shake banana leaf fans and sleep soundly in addition to donating money to buy airplanes.

Legs 164

— Xu Xiaoting

Among the foods to eat, the taste of Jinhua ham is the best!

The grades of legs, in our human race, are white, rough, long and fat, and short and thin. Leg calves inserted in the field to work are the muddy legs of farmers, and long-distance runners are pairs of swift legs.

The beauty of the city and the beauty of the countryside are absolutely contradictory and absolutely different. Rural beauty values muddy legs, while urban beauty loves the snow-white skin of dancers and jade legs that are as smooth and tender as fat.

The radiant red light of the year is shrouded over the heads of lustful men. In this passionate atmosphere, the hearts of men can be tied down by dancers because they are completely seduced by those jade legs. Legs are indeed a mysterious fragment of the human body.

Now that the national crisis is imminent, legs are for people to use, not for people to play with, but the legs of the Chinese people are weak and unenergetic. Since encountering the famous short-legged Japanese people, who have been occupying our country's land step by step, our countrymen only know to leisurely and slowly retreat backward, but do not know to move forward! Those short-legged people have unceremoniously stepped into the three northeastern provinces, stepped into Jehol, and stepped inside the Great Wall. Although they still want to step forward and occupy more, can our countrymen allow him to move forward?

Today, if we want to reverse this declining trend and break this evil environment, indeed, we still need all our countrymen to muster up courage, slap their legs a few times, use our heat and blood to move forward, and fight those short-legged people to the death. I think, although the Japanese are barbaric, they will definitely not be able to withstand our saber cuts and hot blood spurts. The Japanese emperor will not have many fake legs to bestow on his soldiers, like he bestowed on Nomura.

The jade legs of women anesthetize human nature and exploit people's will. Compatriots, compatriots, the national crisis is urgent! You must wake up quickly!

Fasting 165

— Xianxian

When I was young, I read textbooks and remembered the sentences "One day without food is hunger, three days without food is sickness, and seven days without food is death," but I don't know whether Bo Yi and Shu Qi on Shouyang Mountain suffered the exact, no more, no less, full seven days of famine.

Since that time, for two or three thousand years, until modern times, except for those who successfully fasted due to famine years, sieges, lawsuits, and other reasons, going from "hunger" to "sickness" and from "sickness" to "death," it seems that there has not been a third person to join besides Bo Yi and Shu Qi in history.

The Indian Father of the Nation, Mr. Gandhi, was once detained for revolution and fasted, but he endured more than six weeks of starvation. Although "hunger" and "sickness" were successfully completed step by step, he failed at the last moment, finally ending the fast and recovering his health.

Twenty years later, there was a Comrade Niu Lan who played the same trick, but from "hunger" to "sickness," he actually survived the deadline when he should have "died," and gave up his heroic act of fasting, resuming eating bread and drinking milk, and spending his specially preferential prison life.

It is really strange, how can Gandhi and Niu Lan "not die after seven days without food"? It is said that there are reasons for this. The first is because they usually drink goat's milk and cow's milk, which nourish them well, so they don't die, it's not that "their lives shouldn't end." The second is that they don't stop drinking water while fasting, which is also a clever trick. After all, the ancients were not as smart as modern people, and Bo Yi and Shu Qi didn't know this trick, so their "death" was a bit unjust.

Recently, the Indian Father of the Nation, Mr. Gan, has launched a major fast again. But according to the telegram, although he is still Gandhi, who usually drinks goat's milk, and although he still drinks water after fasting, "one day without food" has already made him feel that his stomach is empty, and "three days without food" has already made him so sick that he can hardly move. By the time this article is published, perhaps the "seven days without food" limit has already passed. But I don't know if it can be completed step by step and successfully.

People who have no food to eat desperately want to find food, while people who have status and food to eat insist on fasting. What is the reason? I really don't understand!

People Who Fly Over Walls 166

— Zui Chi Sheng

Chairman Han of Shandong, in order to "promote national martial arts," has specially sought talents who can "fly over walls, strike acupuncture points, and fence with swords," and has set up reward measures. This has aroused discussions among people in society. Some regard it as a joke, and some regard it as an incomprehensible superstition, like a child seeking immortality.

I remember when I was eight or nine years old, around the end of the Qing Guangxu period, my late father, Qiu Ping Gong, was assigned to Jiangsu as a Jinshi, listening to the drums of Wu Gate, and serving as the chief patrol officer of the North Road. He often captured bandits who could fly over walls. Those with great skills could not only fly lightly but also enter the water, hiding in the water for several hours, unharmed, and were nicknamed "Water Crows." These people possessed unique skills, rampaged through the provincial capital, committed numerous crimes, and because they were not easy to capture, the police officers hated them to the bone. At this time, Zhu the Blind (Zhu Zhuzha) served as the judicial commissioner and was very strict in dealing with bandits. Those who captured Water Crows were mostly given extreme punishments. It was really the most unfortunate era for "grassroots heroes."

One night, in the dead of night, a police officer, A, in the mansion was about to go to bed. Suddenly, he heard sounds like footsteps on the roof. He hurriedly called everyone up, and A first went to the drying platform to check. Although I was young, I was driven by curiosity and followed him up. Suddenly, I saw a person in black hiding in a corner, with a sharp blade inserted in his waist. The moonlight was slanted, and I could see him quite clearly. Just as A was about to step forward to arrest him, the person in black suddenly jumped over the river (we lived near the river) and hid on the roof of a shop across the street. Suddenly, there was a hubbub of voices, and everyone used bamboo poles to randomly poke into the air. The black-clothed thief suddenly jumped into the river again. Everyone searched the riverbank, but there were no ripples on the water and no trace of him. After a half-night of disturbance, it was fortunate that there were no losses. Everyone praised the wonder. You think he suddenly soars into the air like a bird, and suddenly enters the water like a swimming fish, like an amphibious animal. This ability of the Water Crow is really not small. Now, when I think about it, it seems like a dream.

These kinds of people who fly over walls are not absent at present. However, most of them have become thieves and have been obscured. Therefore, throughout history, the four words "flying over walls" have been the name for "roaming bandits." Now that Chairman Lu is in this time of national crisis, amidst the sounds of airplanes and cannons, he is actually at ease and wants to invite them out, treat them with the etiquette of distinguished guests. It is probably for "martial arts to save the country," or perhaps it is a method of "preserving national essence"!

Long Novel

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 167

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seven: A Few Words Sever Ties, Shut the Door and Weep Bitterly; One Shoulder Carries Duty, Wine is Shared in Discussion

Ji Zhi originally wanted to laugh, hoping to slip away under the cover of laughter. However, Mrs. Gan's face was devoid of any smile, so how could he make a joke? He had no choice but to take two steps back and sit down on the chair opposite her. Mrs. Gan exhaled smoke and smiled again. Then, pinching the cigarette between two fingers, she tapped the ash with her index finger, aiming for it to fall into the spittoon. She looked at Ji Zhi's face, as if she had a very important question to ask. Although Ji Zhi's mind was clouded with doubts, he naturally did not speak before his sister-in-law said anything. His sister-in-law's smile and look were truly embarrassing. Mrs. Gan said calmly, "Your brother told me that you are engaged to the old Miss Yang. Is that true?" Ji Zhi blushed and said, "That's not true." Mrs. Gan said seriously, "It's true. I'm not joking with you. If you think the old Miss Yang is good, you can get engaged to her. But…" she said, smiling. She held back the rest of her sentence after the word "but." Ji Zhi also said seriously, "It's really not true." Mrs. Gan said, "Don't blame your sister-in-law for scaring you with words. Actually, it's good that you're not engaged to her. Otherwise, your brother would lose his temper. It's not worth sacrificing your career for someone like that. With our family background and your qualifications, can't we find a good wife? Don't worry, within half a year, I'll find you someone as fresh as a flower. But there's one thing: you must break off all contact with the old Miss Yang." Ji Zhi looked at the ground, hesitant, and said in a low voice, "I don't have any contact with her in the first place." Mrs. Gan smiled and said, "You're lying to my face. Your brother saw you at the milk tea shop. You made an appointment with her to talk again in three years, why make such a long appointment?" Ji Zhi knew he couldn't deny it, blushed, and couldn't say a word. Mrs. Gan said, "Your brother came back yesterday, so angry that he couldn't even speak. I asked him many times before he explained. According to him, he wanted to issue an order to remove you from your position. I advised him, saying, 'We're brothers, why get angry? Just talk face to face.'" (74)

Miscellaneous Talk

Nine-Flavored Tea 168

— Zhang Yian

The seats in the third-class tram are almost as comfortable and Westernized as those in Western-style houses. Everything in this carriage is Western-style: the separation of glass and window sashes, the decorative lines and patterns used, the neat, machine-made yellow steel fittings, and even the various advertisements posted are not found in the inland countryside. Moreover, there are constantly moving scenes and various characters outside, and colorful shop windows. A person who has just come from the inland feels a bit dizzy sitting inside, especially since it only costs seven or five copper coins!

Recently, I've noticed that many of the characters used in the Shanghai newspaper articles are different from the original ones. Although the sounds are similar (actually not the same sound, only similar) and the meanings are also similar, there are significant differences from the original meanings. For example, "slightly" is sometimes written as "slightly," "advantages and disadvantages" as "fierce," "smart" as "clever," and "street gossip" as "street language," and so on. I don't know if the writers are deliberately changing them to show novelty, or if they can't remember the original characters for a moment and are temporarily writing out similar sounds with meanings that can be understood.

Dreams seem to be more extreme than reality. If it is a rational dream, even a very ordinary thing can feel very serious in the dream. If it is an emotional dream, it is mostly related to sadness. Even a very slight touch can make you greatly sad, even making you cry so hard that you can't breathe. Although you don't find many tears flowing when you wake up, you are already extremely grief-stricken in the dream. (Later, I discovered that when I have such dreams, nine times out of ten it's because my mouth and nose are covered by the quilt, suffocating my breath, hence the dream.) As for encountering bandits and ferocious beasts, being persecuted, and even being killed, I have experienced them all in dreams, and more than once.

If there were no young people for ten years, and everyone was either young children or adults above a certain age, I wonder what the state of romance would become.

As long as you are willing to shout until your voice is hoarse, there will definitely be the first person to applaud, and then everyone else will follow.

In the books that I love to read, I like them to have some advertisements for other books. These advertisements are not annoying, as long as the books they introduce have equal value and similar nature to the book I am currently enjoying, but don't post irrelevant advertisements.

Excessive desires are like a bright moon hanging in space. Although it cannot be said that the moon is a place that humans cannot reach, if someone could reach it, it would be an extraordinary event.

The Peking Opera theater symbolizes the entire Chinese society. Peking Opera is the crystallization of Chinese drama, and the state of the Peking Opera theater is the crystallization of Chinese society. As long as the situation in the Peking Opera theater improves a little, China will probably not be invaded by others.

It's a pity that the washed-up leading actor is now only playing an unimportant role in the front row.

Running errands is really boring.

Even if there are no exciting dramas, several plays still have to be staged at the beginning, because the old officials in the troupe need to eat, and the other unimportant roles and even the extras need to eat as well.

Mutual love is like colored flowers, plants, and bird feathers, with rich reds and lush greens, naturally pleasing to people. Unrequited love is like light ink landscape paintings, although simple and unadorned, their quality can sometimes be higher than that of colored paintings.

Unsuccessful and short-lived love is like a short story; momentary events that seem like love but are not are like a piece of miscellaneous thoughts, each with its own intriguing aspects.

Age will cancel your happiness.

Because I am over thirty years old, talking about love feels a bit embarrassing.

Some people say that married people are not worthy of talking about love, and people with children should not talk about love even more. Others say that marriage and love are not the same thing, and children have nothing to do with love.

Important News

Presidents of Various Universities in Peiping Visit He Yingqin

Safety Issues for Business Students 169

▲ He Instructed Them to Return to School and Continue Classes as Usual

(Peiping, 17th) The presidents of the four universities—Xu Songming of Peiping University, Jiang Menglin of Peking University (represented by Wang Lie), Mei Yiqi of Tsinghua University, and Li Zheng of Normal University—visited He Yingqin this afternoon. He instructed them to return to school and continue classes as usual, addressing the safety concerns of business students.

Gu Cheng, the president of the Women's College of Arts and Sciences, returned to Peiping yesterday and stated that although the Boxer Indemnity funds had been used, the educational expenses for Peiping and Tianjin could still be allocated as usual. There are no security issues in Peiping, and the intention to move the women's college to Kaifeng has been cancelled.

Ministry of Education Commends Donations to Support Education 171

▲ The Ge Brothers

Ge Fengqi and Ge Fenggang, renowned pigment merchants in Shanghai, have been donating funds since the fifth year of the Republic of China to establish the private Tire Ren School in Qingyang, Jiangyin, and have been covering all expenses incurred over the years, amounting to a total of 80,000 yuan to date. After receiving the report, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, recognizing the Ge brothers' enthusiasm for education and their commendable dedication, specifically requested the Ministry of Education to commend them to encourage them. The Ministry of Education has now instructed the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, stating that Jiangsu citizens Ge Fengqi and Ge Fenggang are enthusiastic about education and have generously donated substantial funds, which is highly commendable. In addition to publicizing their actions in the official gazette and promoting them, the National Government should issue a commendation decree at the end of the year and grant them each a first-class certificate for donating funds to support education, to encourage them.

News from the Ministry of Education 172

The Ministry of Education recently recorded the following news: (1) A submission to the Executive Yuan requesting, based on approval document No. 1548, that starting from May of this year, the monthly silver tax revenue of 25,000 yuan to be received by the Ministry of Education according to the original plan not be subject to monthly allocation by the Zhejiang Provincial Government.
